Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, if it lies low for a long time.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is drained, if it is scraped off without leaving the peel which contains that moisture, because it returns to its place when left alone; then put cotton in Egyptian style, if it is present; if not, in water and oil, and apply the bandage, and leave it until the other side is healed; and this will correct what is delayed that remains hurt
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And thus when the cotton has returned, as before, the second layer, and the third, until you are certain that it has not moved at night; then cure the wound appropriately, as is suitable.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the dressing sticks to the wound, if you follow this form, for a long time; and you wipe your fingers, and the eschar from all parts, and put all your cure to pull out the cloth or where it lies; and if the artery opposes you, do as I have said afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And do the same with the abscess if it is purulent, and if you cut and cure as I have said
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the size of the abscess is more liquid, because it is a matter of blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if there are any abscesses or swellings or if there is no moisture, and if these are old abscesses that I cauterise or swellings of a woman of childbearing age; and if I find the abscess just like a stone, rough and white, and cannot burst; and if nothing is done about it, it will cause just as much damage as if it were a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses which arise from the head of the shoulder and the root of the ear, it is because these arise from the swelling of the head of the shoulder and the root of the ear; it will burst every day the most dependent part of the limb; and they must be treated as is fitting.</start_of_turn>
des scrophules	And the size of the wound on the hairy part and the moisture, if it is slight, for they are of little blood. And if any of these wounds or heads or there is no moisture, and of these wounds which I cauterize or heads of an old woman; and find the wound just like a stone, rough and white, and cannot break. And if there is no blood in it, we must make just as good a wound as with a stone. In other wounds which come from the head or from the ears, forasmuch as these which come from the head of the children and have roots of the ears, they open if they be at all days the most dependent limb, for to stir the joint; and they cure as they should.
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times this abscess appears at the collarbone, and the armpits, and in the groin, and never in any other place or limb, and is bloody, and is joined to each other.</start_of_turn
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And if a swelling is properly deep within its coat, if like a knot and has its origin at the root, as we have said; and the appearance of these swellings is many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are many cases where the swelling contains moisture, and if there are malignants that do not obey the laws of health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In those cases where you see a good bone structure at the touch, and which is similar in color to bone, and dry in parts and not moist as when there is pus in the neck or in the artery or the vein, and is not deep; if you must handle it, grasp it by the lower lip and the heel of the thumb as we have said in the apostemes of the head; and withdraw little by little, and be careful not to tear the nerves or veins, or to cause swelling or bruising, but only to grasp what you must grasp
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	If you burn the vein or an artery and it will not allow you to work, put in the wound a piece of vitriol glass shard, or some powder that remains bloodless, and strain the wound; and leave it until the swelling subsides, and soften the wound, and begin to move.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	If the blood is not stained, if you return to your work until you have completed it; then if there appear any small abscesses, cope and crush them.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	If there is a large abscess at the root of the vein, if you cannot do anything but only cope the abscess at its root, but hold it with a strong double thread, and leave it hanging free; then apply pressure to the wound with a bundle of cotton soaked in Egyptian balsam, and cure it.</start_of_turn
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	If you support the entire swelling, if you command that the two edges of the wound be reunited and held now, then there will be no further swelling due to the size of the swelling.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	If you command that you understand to cover the root of the swelling, and to bear, and to reunite as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those swellings which cause swelling perceive either death or opening; and perceive with that which has been said before, depending, and bring together again what is diminished by corruption; and when the wound is well cleansed, if the ointment cure which is healing properly, as long as it remains healthy.</start_of_turn
de squinance	When the wound is sufficiently drained, if you apply an ointment of benzoin, as long as it is healthy.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancient ones spoke of the breadth of the throat; but I have never seen it done in our land, and this is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	As for those who stammer, it is necessary that the epiglottis, which is called the 'voice box', be freed; and this will not help, for all the veins and arteries in the body rise up towards the patient at the time of speaking, or in the throat or at the root of the tongue.</start_of_turn>
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the windpipe, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to prevent the loss that comes from the strangulation.</start_of_turn
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is commanded therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it from three circles or four at most, between the two circles or by the quantity of the cut so that it does not reach the cartilage; and if it is covered by the section of the epiglottis that there is no swelling, and the blood vessels are long enough.</start_of_turn
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	If the master is fearful, if you can, extend the skin of the throat to the chin; then cut the skin as far as the nail; avoid the blood vessels, if you see nothing; and then close the wound as we have said; and demonstrate by the section of the smoke of the nail that the spurge has escaped from the broken bone, and by the loss of voice; and leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed since it was doubted that the strangulation is present, assemble the four limbs of the wound together at the corners, and hold them all steady with the cartilage; then administer medicines which cause the formation of scar tissue, as long as it is necessary.</start_of_turn>
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	But if the throat is still swollen, it does not make this juice until the patient is dead, and the fault lies with the physician.</start_of_turn>
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Therefore, close the epiglottis so that the patient does not suffocate; and he breathes through the wound; and thus is preserved from death; and for this reason the ancients command that the wound be left open until the malice of the disease has passed, which takes three days or four; and then they command that the wound be closed and healed, until it is healed; and I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw a woman who had swallowed a knife, and plunged it into her throat, and cut part of the windpipe; and I went to call for help, and found her as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had escaped from it, and it was well that there was no vessel or conduit except the throat that had been injured by the wound.</start_of_turn
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hastened, and closed the wound, and cured it until it healed; and the woman did not feel any pain, and returned to her senses; for in the cutting of the epiglottis, I did not find any fear
de la grosse gorge	of the great gorge.</start_of_turn
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	These abscesses are called "throat hernia", and are large abscesses in the color of butter, and are much in women; and there are two kinds: natural and accidental; or naturally there is no reason.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental kind is in two ways: one is similar to fat, and the other is like an abscess that comes from an artery; and there is fear, and one must not attempt to do anything fierce except in small things, and prove and seek throughout: if you find it as thick as grease, and cannot go into any vein, if you cut it, as we cut flesh, and carry it away with all its hair, if there is none; and embrace it well round, and cure it as it should be, until it is perfectly healed
des nous	And encircle all around thoroughly, and cure it as it should be, until it is perfectly healed.
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many ways of us exist, of which I shall speak; and behold that I shall tell you all the difference that is between health and sickness.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that dislocation is caused by heat and fever that persists, as long as the fever has not passed, and is accompanied by swelling; therefore rest the fever and heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With neither pain nor fever nor chill, and contains I syfac, which is its own sac and is according to the colour of gold, and begins like butter, and becomes fat; and are according to its semblance, or fat, or moist, and the colour is such as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of the wound, that you first inquire about the instrument which is called the “entrant,” according to its form or chapter which follows.</start_of_turn
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the method of the investigation of abscesses of the body is that you take or more moisture than you find in the abscess, and twist your thumbs and fingers, until you feel that the instrument has perceived the knot, then that it is according to the greatness of the abscess; then withdraw the needle, and take care of that the wound does not burst
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture covers the area to be cauterized, let it remain until it has dried. If after removing the cautery the surrounding area does not bleed, then if necessary make an incision in the form of a cross, grasp it firmly with forceps, and cautiously remove it from the root with the fingers; if you do not handle it with care, if you break it into pieces, nothing will remain.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	If nothing remains, if it returns several times; if some remains, if you grieve not, if you apply to the wound some corrosive powders, tighten the wound, and put on soothing things around the cautery; and if it is great, if you cut out two fingers of the wound, and cure what is burdensome.</start_of_turn>
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein beats contrary to you or otherwise if you are in a hurry, and employ broken vitriol, and leave it for three or four days, until the wound has healed, and rest the inflammation of blood; then return to the covering that was removed when it has healed
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the forms of the instruments that are introduced within, and there are three kinds: great, medium, and small; and there are three quarters which are called "albaret", and one which is called "breb", and there are three kinds: great, medium, and small, for enclosing fistulas; and they are like needles which are used to sew up wounds, and are of saffron, iron, or silver, and must be yellow, and are more proven with black pitch for enclosing fistulas; and there are three kinds: great, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the large size of the perforation.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of the instruments are like those of seeds, as you see here: great, medium, and small; and if the instruments have two curves of three kinds each; and if the instruments have three curves, and are of three kinds each; and if the instruments have two curves, and an instrument with only one curve, and are of three kinds each; all these are necessary for their use
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of the humerus is fractured, and some of them are so severe that they do not cut through the vein or nerve; and from these intruders are the bones that are placed in sleeves, so that the patient does not lose them when the abscesses are opened; and there are three kinds: great, small, and medium, as you see; and they are used only in cases of fracture, such as the limb, arm, forearm, and heel, and in similar cases. And no other instrument is ever used except for hooks resembling fistulas, according to this fashion, in order to hold the blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And he must never be put back in the place where he has already bled from veins, arteries, or in any other way whatsoever.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	In no case do the bones of the armpits of certain people become swollen when they begin to decay, so that they appear like female breasts; and remain limp and floppy, and who sees them cured, if it is not by soaking them according to this fashion from line b to g inclusive.
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape the fat, and apply the medical plaster firmly; then sew the two layers of the wound together with sutures, and cure until it is healed; and if the mother suckles clingly, and is eased by her greatness, as with women, if there are two ribs below, by two similar incisions; so that one is holding the other at the end of one and the other, so that the greater line contains the lesser following this form, from this line .b. up to the line .g.; then scrape the skin between the two layers, and bone the fat, and insert what has been said of sutures and powders, and what is necessary for the cure, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not completely made, because the patient does not want to rest, or for the discharge of blood, if it is necessary, fill the wound with moist cotton wool in corrosive order.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of boils</start_of_turn>
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from boils are often caused by hard scrofula or when there are ribs, and there is only contenance of moisture.</start_of_turn
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	If there is moisture contained, it is to be cut according to this form, from line b to line g.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When all the surrounding tissues in the abscess are emptied, if the wound has a great deal of cotton, leave it in place until the other side is reached, then extract all the cotton, and cure the wound that arises from this until it is healed.

If the abscess has the appearance of boils, if it is as we have said in the treatment of boils, and if the wound opens again, if necessary perform cautery as we have previously said.</start_of_turn>
de la routure de l’artere	of the root of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	If the artery is closed, and the skin is tough that is above, if there are many abscesses in coming, and also blood escapes from the vein and abscesses; if one knows that it is for the artery, if the abscesses are long and burst; and if one knows that it is for the vein, if there is swelling of the limb. It is foolish to close this abscess; and just as when one has pulled out the nails and the hairs and the heel and the teeth and other bones, and the mouth is wide open.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. des apostemes des ners	Des apostemes des ners.

des grosses boces pendans	From the armpits downwards.

For when you cure the whole, if it is not firmly held, the head of the shoulder will not be perceived; and comes blackening and corruption to its root and bone; if you cover all that is black and corrupt, then apply honey and flour made from pomegranate peel and sometimes, cure with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if blood flows away, if you mix the lunar cautery in this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery has two helpful dispositions together: that is, at the flow of blood, and at the corruption; and if the head of the shoulder is corrupted and drawn back, if you bite or pull out the hair a thumb's breadth, and the patient urinates; and when the hair is loosened from the root which has not been circumcised, or there is wound or incision, if you then pinch it with the instrument which chews, until the ligament is untied, and deliver the head of the shoulder from all parts; and if this should grieve you, if you then pinch at the spleen or navel, without any wound on the head of the shoulder or the nail; then dry well between them, and put on a bandage of moist linen to the cold.
de la circoncision	When the circumcision is complete...
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not merely a continuation of other wounds; however, when we perform this work of our own free will, and do it properly, if it is necessary that our workers do the best work, and the most gentle for health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the old folk do not tell me of circumcision of their sons, for they do not use it in their law, and we have learned only what we have learned through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen the greatest part of masters and physicians who performed circumcision on young children, with force, and with a new knife; but when the testicles burst because of two layers, or by chance if one cuts these off and leaves the other behind.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or the recovery is painful, and the pain is doubled, and there is the mutilation which is from no certain origin, and the point of the limb is not securely bound; and by the mutilation of the cord by chance escapes the wound, and completes the work, and many times they are born again without any mutilation, and I have seen it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the alteration which is made against the power of all the threads, I have found the benefit of the experiment, for the forces tear just as well downwards as upwards.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you press your hand, if it is equally taut in all directions, but the thread is well twisted around the leather; and if the thumb is stiff from the first movement, as if you are making the child understand, do not force it to lie only on the thread around the nail, but rather make it slip in every way you can; then make it rest between your hands straight, and bring the forces between your hands or remove your fingers so that the child cannot see them, neither any instruments; then tighten your hand at the nail and puff or groan, and draw it up as high as the head of the nail; then keep it well bound with ordure that is assembled, then bind the thread with a double thread, then bind it again so that there are two knots at the pouch and the index finger, and clip between the two threads, then hold the thumb down firmly and draw the chief of the nail; then leave the blood to flow freely, because that is the remedy; and put powder on and over the powder I drape a bandage glued with a piece of egg yolk moistened with rose oil and fresh, and leave it on until the next morning, and treat it in the same way until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	When the forces are formed in abundance in this way: two arms should be tense and firm, and the arms should be as great as the hand equal in size:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the forces is when the cords of the incision are too taut; therefore it is necessary to extend the nails beyond the incision, even though it makes a wound; and to grasp them equally, and if you cannot hold them at your nails, if you have to hold them, and then grasp them.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they trespass two days, and what is below the ribcage is inflamed, if you leave them as long as the spasms subside and the skin is lightly scorched; if you touch them as you please, and hold the lower part of the ribcage, it will do them no good.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And thus cure the wound of things soaked in powder, which we have said or treated with powder; and if you touch them too much, it will go away, if it does not do any good; cure it thus, as we have said, until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
dou retenement de l’urine	because of the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The urine is retained if the stone, or blood clot, or bile, or barley, or some other thing, which we have mentioned in the division, is in the bladder; and if the urine is not drained, and you see that the stone is in the bladder neck or the bladder itself, if you can make the patient hunch over his knees; and let the pieces of the stone go out through the back, and extend the belly from the part below the back, and restrain the patient as much as you can; and then grasp the bladder neck at the expression of the stone upwards, so that the urine is drained out; and if it does not come out, as we have mentioned, and the patient feels great pain, if you can, administer extraction with all the instruments that are called "siringues"; thus is the form: either of hammered silver legier with a rounded head like a goose feather; or the caine of a palm half long; or legier.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And thus the method of extracting urine is this: if you take a single thread doubled, and bind one end to the head of the bladder or belly, and pass the other end through the tube; then drain the excess cloth and pass until it reaches the head of the tube. Then join the tube with oil or butter and egg-white, and make the patient sit on the edge of the seat. Then raise the bladder and the belly with oil moistened with olive oil and tepid water; then gently insert the tube into the belly, until it reaches the root of the belly, then double the belly upwards towards the buttocks. Then withdraw the tube before it reaches the bladder, and let the patient urinate until the bladder is empty. This must not be done except in the case that the thread or the urine itself is twisted; then hold the thread at both ends and the urine will follow the thread, and when it is withdrawn force must be used, and correct the urine. Then repeat the tube until the bladder is empty and the patient is aligned.
des maladies de la vessie	Des maladies de la vessie.
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When bladder stones or blood comes into the bladder, or when it is filled, and you see urine and medicine being distilled, if you do everything that is called the "clepsedre," which is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	She is closed, and if there are three punctures: two on one side and one on the other, as you see; and the liquid spurts from the root as the doctor has noticed; and when we can manage to drain the moisture, and push as much as is necessary; and when you see the medicine dripping into the bladder, put the chief surgeon over the moisture and draw out the one who is inside; if you draw out the moisture from the surgeon, and then push him back violently; if the moisture enters again, and comes to the bladder, if the patient feels it; and that is the form of a subtle cluster from which we cluster the bladder.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	It is of silver or gold, and the head is higher; and from the first vein or the groin there is a vein; then take a bladder of mutton and put the moisture into which you see clustering the bladder, and tie between the two breasts a strong double thread, and burn one half of that moisture over the fire; then draw out the chief of the cluster from the root, and strain your hand over the bladder until the patient feels that the moisture has come to the bladder; and if you do not have a bladder, if you take a piece of parchment, and make a circle, and pierce it roundly around; then draw the thread strongly through these punctures, and assemble the circle as if you were assembling a ball, and put inside what you see of oil, moisture, and water, and tie it to the instrument; and do as you would with a bladder, pressing your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	De la piere.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already mentioned in the division the methods for cutting stone, and the extraction of the same with medicines; and I have mentioned the difference between a bruised stone and a solid one, and the signs of each; and in what case a stone must be cut of a certain size; and in the bladder, and in the gut; and I will tell you openly and briefly.</start_of_turn>
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that a stone which is bruised in the bladder is often accompanied by vomiting, and this is a sign that the stone is in great pain in its entirety; and it causes the patient to spit blood, and to suffer great pain in the flanks, and to vomit many times, and then becomes hardened; and from these vomits there is always some sediment; and it is light for the healing of these vomiting spells until they are three years old, and is more grievous in old people, and is like a young man between youth and old age; and the cure for these is lighter than for those who have a large stone.</start_of_turn
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, if it is necessary, first purify the patient by vomiting, in order to remove all the poison that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it never hinders to inquire about the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the hands, and loosen and move downwards, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and does not go up again; then make him sit between your hands openly, and his hands rest on his thighs, so that the bladder is all declining downwards; then question and touch within; if you feel the stone in the space, then hurry now to cut above the stone.</start_of_turn>
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not spit out on touching throughout, then moisten your left index finger, if the patient is old, or your middle finger, if the patient is young and robust; and press down to the base, and question the stone, and when you feel it in your finger, if the bladder is against the navel; then press above your finger, and the stone will come out spontaneously or you will see it spit out.</start_of_turn
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend with his right hand the hairs on high, and with his left hand grasp the skin that is between the hairs in the part where we make the incision; then insert the spatula covering the area that is like this.
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And between what is between the buttocks and the navel, do not enter more than halfway but at the cost of the left nipple; and be straight on the stone, and two either adjoin or support the stone, and be the size that it will traverse if it is wide by reason of its breadth, and narrow within, according to the quantity of the stone, do not make it too large; for by chance the press if it must be on the stone or support, that it leap forward in its work; and strings that are torn from the stone or have angles, and margins: if it is grasped to the ischium; and if there is something squeezed, it is like a nut, round, from which issue is slight.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	And so if there are angles and margins, make the size greater; and if it does not leap, it is understood that you must pull on the tendons that are as sharp as a file at the head, because it is necessary to pull out the stone if it does not escape; or you can use a curved instrument at the head; and if you do not manage to engage it, if the stone is large, or if it slips out, if it is the straining of vitriol; and if there are several stones, pull out the largest one at the belly of the bladder first, then put on the rest, and then pull out the main one, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are any.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is great swelling, if you cover it, it makes a greater wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	Or if these two things happen to the patient: he dies, or the urine comes out together by the leak of the urine; but whatever you do to try to stop it, or to drain the tension, as long as you tear it out piece by piece; and when you have completed your work, if you apply incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and tighten it, and put above it a wet cloth in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the burnt abscess; then restore the patient to his shoulder and do not loosen the band until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have loosened it, if there is too much moisture in the wound, then cure with oil and vinegar, and with basilicon ointment, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if pus comes out in the wound and corruptions, and congestion of blood in the bladder, or either because the urine is retained, which is known in part like that without jumping with the urine: bring forth your dose in the wound, and drain that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and carry it away; then raise the wound with water and ease and bandage, and help in every way that you know how, until he is healed; and know that all the times that you cure him, that you bind up the two seams and collect the medicines above the limb.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	If the stone is small and it is in the bladder or the urethra, and it is fixed in place, and the urine cannot pass; if the physician does what I have said above, that you must urinate many times, we will hear of the size of this cure.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proven this in this case
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take hold of the iron according to this form and be at a right angle, with two angles fixed in one basin:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.
