If it is broken and spurts with the urine, and is stained with blood; and if you cannot do this for any reason, then I take a thread from the bladder and another from above, and I pass the bladder through the stone between the two lines; and I pull it out forcefully, and I loosen the thread, and I congeal the blood that is in the wound; and the cure until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
de la piere des femmes	If you are unable to translate the line, please leave the line empty.
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	When the bone is swollen in women, and this happens only once, the cure is grief, and is defended by two things: the first is that the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman who knows herself very well, even though she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And thus the third method, if by chance one cannot find a woman who is truly skilled in this work of hands; and the fourth method, if the woman’s stone is more prominent than the man’s, for it can make a deeper incision, and great danger there is. And if it is necessary to do this, if one must take a lesser woman, and mark the navel on her, and if one does not find it, no further inquiry is of any use; and present to her a woman who is wise in life, or a woman who knows a part of this work, and command her to do what you command of her by inquiry of the stone; and see well whether the woman is a virgin: for if she is, she can push out the stone or foundation and ask for the stone; and if she finds it, if she confines the stone again, command her to hold the stone or with the patient, and press her left hand on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If that be true, if it be moved from the groin to the knee, as far as it comes to the root of the thigh; then seize upon the stone at the root of the thigh and find the middle of the bone there where it appears; and feel the thigh in that part. And do not move the thigh above the knee or below, but keep it at its first small size. Then withdraw the hand gradually to the size, if you feel the thigh is relaxed as much as the bone can bear, and discharge the urine as many times as you have need of it.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if there are many discharge the urine, it is known to be an issue.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if it does not go away, if you put on the hand of vitriol and keep it there for an hour until it is stained; then return to your work, until the bone is healed, and have the instruments that I told you about in the extraction of the stone as your companions; and if it does not go away, and it is the artery that is cut, if you put on the powder on the hand and strain it with sponges and wool, and do not attempt it again, and leave the bone alone, only by chance does the patient recover; then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the bleeding has ceased and the limb is relaxed, if you return to your work while the stone remains fixed.
de hernie carnouse	De hernie carnouse.
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramice aquouse is nothing else but an assembly of moisture or white fat, which is as soft as the seeds of coriander, that contains the egg; and it is called "syfac," and never is it properly in the yolk of the egg, if we take care that this is not another exercise; and it is the skin of the seed between the white fat that we have said. And these things do not happen by chance.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this marrow is from weakness that comes from the seeds, and it is spread throughout that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And never if percussion comes upon the bones, this moisture is of many colors: either a declining color to jaundice, or without redness, or black, or pale blue, and this is more; and these are signs of corruption in this assembly, for if it is white or pale as we have said, if the abscess is ripe and long as the figure of an egg, and it does not open the bones, because it has moisture throughout.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the very flesh, if the abscess is ripe with a part of the egg, and because of this people think that this is an egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the bones and the white substance, if it feels soft; then when you see the color of the moisture, if it shows throughout the whole surrounding area, from which it is formed as before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this, therefore, which follows the introductor, judge of that which is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we bind them with iron, if it be known that the patient is sound in spirit and flesh; then we apply a bandage above the shoulder, above something high, and place upon him a cushion of cloth; then we sit on his left side, and command the minister to sit on his right, and extend the arm up to the second rib from the breastbone; then we take the sponge, and with the needle pierce the skin among the ribs from the long side until the navel, and make a complete incision dividing the skin of the ribs up to the white fat; and we burn off the fat secretly as it comes; then we pierce the navel with a needle, and drain all the fluid, and then put in our sponges, and withdraw the needle; and do not touch the breastbone, but only the navel; cut off everything or in pieces immediately the cost of it secretly, for if you do not cut it well, the fluid will return; and if the urine spurts from your work, retain it in its place until you have completed the work of the navel. Then assemble the two ribs of the breastbone at their joint, and cure it as with the other wounds, until it is sound.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the abscess corrupted by another disease, if you must tie up the veins that are suspended, doubting the discharge of blood; then cut off the abscess at its source, drain out the abscess, and cure it like we have said.</start_of_turn
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the wound is large enough to be assembled into two parts together, its edges are like two branches; if you have made the other part just as before, then wipe away the blood, and put into the wound a layer of lint soaked in rose oil; and put over that another layer of lint soaked in wine and oil, and put on the two edges, and put over them doubled cloths, and bind it up according to this fashion.
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths, and use coarse wool yarn like this in appearance and join them together at the groin; and one of the heads grasps on the foundation almost up to the back, and the other at the part below the navel; and the other two fingers grasp the two angles, and everything is put together with a strong bandage
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And so you must do in all ways that you can, until you have removed all; and keep that the fire does not touch the egg; and take that this work is more salve; and measure carefully the amount of blood, and more cautiously the work of the size; and if anything opposes you, or incisions or discharges of blood or anything else, if you can cure what opposes you, according to what is before said.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is pale and does not wish to endure this work because of its horror, if you fear perforation, as I have said, and you are certain by the signs that we have said that the aquous solution is lax, if you make the patient sit on a low chair; then pierce the abscess at the lower part with a broad needle, and make the perforation long and deep; and if the wound is large, let the blood flow freely; then put a bandage on the wound and bind it, and leave the remaining blood to drain away naturally; and cure it until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not stop the bleeding in the wound, it is to be understood that you must drink a penny or the instrument with which the hydropic is treated, as it is said above; and expand the wound and make sure that the blood returns, and reassemble after six months or when it is convenient, and when it is reassembled as before, the patient will be able to recover his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the buttocks.
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	The hair that grows in this part of the limb has doubt and fear in many; for it seems that it is worth leaving it alone; and I will tell you the work and the signs of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	Therefore, when an abscess comes or bursts, and there are wounds; this is by chance.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is known by excess of pain and swelling, which is spread over the joints, or by percussion; and the colour of the abscess is like that of old gold; and there is no pain, and it is an abscess of grief; and by chance it is a bloody abscess, foul and painful, and of dark colour, and does not arise from any artery, or from swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is not from an artery, if it is known by the position of the abscess, when you press it down with your hand; and do not touch it otherwise
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who is made of swelling of a vein is known by his disposition at the expression of touch of the two thumbs, and can well make the size above this semblance, and above the other charges; and that you cope low like a coion, then the egg is high, and the thread is white syfac, and deliver the suspensoire from all parts of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the egg is already sowed with these charges which are not needed, if you must therefore trace the egg, and cope; and if it is towards the syfac, or in what is in the vessels, if you must deliver all that is tense, and cope roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if it is on the surface of the face, or within the blood vessels, it is recommended that you deliver all that is tense, and gently round the edges.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is finished, if you have used up the wool bandage in oil and rose wine, then cure with other treatments until it is healed
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the buttocks.
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess enclosed by a covering resembling a bean, with the softening of the coions, and the patient groans greatly when he walks; and the cure for this disease is well near as poor as this one which we have said before, and all that you will hear of this work is the work of the old men, according to what they make of it
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	You must make the patient sit down on a low seat, then support the shoulder blade between your thumbs and index fingers of both hands, and grasp firmly at the waist. Then cut across the shoulder blade through the bones, as far as necessary, and remove the marrow. Then insert a needle or string with a double thread and pass it through the first hole or where the bone has fractured, and tie at the other end. Then sew the wound neatly, according to the length of the wound, and remove the corrupt marrow. Then cure the wound like any other, or apply pressure to stop bleeding if necessary, so that no vessel has been damaged. For if all the vessels have been damaged, it is better to remove the shoulder bones from all the bones; if it is possible to do so without losing the patient’s sensibility.
de la routure dou syfac	If the oesophagus does not regain its nourishment from the incision of the blood vessels, and dries and does not seek help.
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The coming of this root is by cut or by incision above the belly at the flanks, or by extension of the intestines from that passage to one of the hips; and this passage is either by cut or by extension of the intestines, and comes from these two modes of motion: by percussion, or by leap, or by pressure, or by elevation of grief, and by like things; and the signs when it is by cut of the flanks are that there are many wounds and that they are long in tension and do not come immediately; and the abscesses are equal up to the navel, because the flanks press on the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the sign is that when the jaw is fractured, it causes sudden pain, and the teeth are diversely exposed, from the soft tissue, and this is due to the bursting of the intestines and the hardness of the jaw.</start_of_turn
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never do the bones move with the intestine, and is retained when it is pressed, and causes great suffering to the patient, even when it is pressed.</start_of_turn
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these fiery cures with fear, for it is known to flee.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	When the intestines are coming out through the cut or by incision above the belly at the flanks, or by extension from that passage to one of the hips; this passage is either by cut or by extension of the intestines, and comes from these two modes of motion: by percussion, or by leap, or by pressure, or by elevation of grief, and like things. The signs when it is by cut of the flanks are that there are many wounds and that they are long in tension and do not come immediately; the abscesses are equal up to the navel because the flanks press on the intestines.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never shall the area be cauterized beyond what has been said, after the incision, in doubt of the discharge of blood.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For in this work, there often occurs blood loss, leaving the limb long as it is; and if it lingers too long, whether from a sudden swelling or from an acute fever, do what we have said, until it is loose; then treat the wound with another remedy, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	De hernie carnouse.
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this chapter, I have never seen anyone cure with fire.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	The old people say it is like the branch which binds the nut, in part as you bind the blood vessels, after the size above lightly to the outside; then break it in two, and treat the abscess of what has burst, until the blood vessels cease bleeding; and treat it as we have said, until it is perfectly healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes blood flows out like mad, as we have said, and opens the wound; and do not cut any intestines as long as they are bound, and if you do, that is bad, and repair it immediately; and every time it lingers too long in this place, if you believe the wound or swelling, until the intestines are cut; and this is because of the swelling of the spleen, as we have said, because it is extended, then is softened and relaxed the wound and open; and treat it as we have said before.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you have closed the wound, if the pus and blood drain from the wound, as long as it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The scab is restrained, and has no mark in the course of treatment, and the cautery is mute in this place, and more proximate to health.</start_of_turn>
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the leather of the nails</start_of_turn
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times is the leather of the nails softened in warm homes, because the nails that are within are softened, and it is seen; and it is necessary, when we see it being cured, to make the patient lie on his back, and to soften the leather that is softened on the natural leather; then join the layers together with a suture, and if you see, close the excess of softened leather with two or three stitches firmly; then close between the stitches, and cure as the others, until it is healed, and cut the thread.</start_of_turn>
dou chastrement	Dou chastrement
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	The wounds which are scraped out in our law, and for this reason I do not wish to speak of them in this book; and it is not necessary to force them except in two ways: the first is that the witness of the wound testifies when required, and describes the wound; and the other, because we have often seen these wounds made by beasts in our service, as for example, oxen, sheep, cats and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that scrapes are done in two ways: by traction or by cutting
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the traction method, we seat the beast in warm water, until the wound is softened and painless; then we grasp the wound with your hand, until it is set and no longer causes pain
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	From the limb: Command that you hold firmly, and press the skin of the toes to your left hand, then bind the suspension, and seize each finger at the base, when you have well supported them; and leave no trace of pain or swelling which remains on the vessels; and this method of cautery is milder than that which is made by traction, because by traction remains by chance no part of the toes, for which the best desire is luxury; then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	des hermofrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphroditism is in two ways as at home: one if between the two testicles appears as the figure of the nature of a woman, or if there is hair, and sometimes in the court it urinates.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other kind is in women, and has on the navel as a beard and two testicles
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for tumors and boils is that you cut off all the surrounding carbuncles, and treat them like other wounds; in the second method, for those who urinate through the skin of their genitals, if there is no other cure.
de la tentigene	Hermaphroditism is in two ways: one if between the two testicles opens just like the figure of the nature of a woman, or if there is hair, and sometimes in the urine is excreted between the testicles. And the other way if in women, and has on the navel just like a beard and two testicles. And the cure of the envy and fame is if you cut out all the testicles, and the cure is like other wounds; in the second way, of men whose urine leaps through the skin of the testicles, if there is no cure.
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	The ailment is a carbuncle that lies on the natural part, as long as it is too large to see; and many women have had as much pain as if it were a hand, and this is the cure.</start_of_turn>
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary that you hold the excess of the ailment at your hand or arm and cut it off lightly; and do not be too rough, for bleeding will not come; then the cure is like any other cure as long as it is healthy; and at another wound that comes from the mouth of the marrow, and the marrow, and by chance spurts out, and this is called the ancient "coward's disease".</start_of_turn
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you are certain that you have set it, as we have said, hold the limb firm until it is healed.
de erratique	De erratique.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	If the nature of the woman is not fully understood, or if the perforation is small; or if it is by birth or accident of illness that it has come to be; or if it is from a clot of blood, or a subtle or thick pus, and is made by the uterus, or in the ribs, or the spleen, or anything similar; and if the conception is suspected, and the birth has occurred, or by chance the flowers have fallen out; and if the woman has known of such things.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the limbs are swollen close to the surface, if there is swelling to the two sides or to the right.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a subtle pus, and if it is close to two fingers, if you are in a hurry, and burst: put your two index fingers together, and the woman should be on her back, spread out her legs; then press the two fingers together until the subtle pus is round, and is above the swelling; then take hold of the pus, and mix it with oil, and put it on the limb, and keep the woman still until it has healed.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the scapula is hard and thick, it is fitting that you should grasp the spur resembling a berry of myrtle.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is deep and wide, if you suspend it with a bandage and grasp; and have medicines that stop bleeding, such as acaice, dragon's blood, incense, and eggs; then mix in a dose of lead plaster, so that the wound does not stick together; and let it be long, and mix in a little dried lint; and so be cured of other cures until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when there is a deep wound, if you cover it as described above, except for abscesses that are inflamed.</start_of_turn
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For the abscess that is in the marrow, do not touch it with fire.</start_of_turn
des emorroides	des emorroides.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Emorroydes are openings of veins which, without caution, are usually fatal; and when the hemorrhoids are old, they become thelul. And we have already mentioned in the division the signs and symptoms, and I will say here those which resolve the cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and thelul, when they are inflamed in the marrow, and do not appear to the sense, if not treated by fire.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those which are at the mouth of the marrow, we can feel, are those which we can cure
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then hold the abscess tightly, and press it to its root, then sprinkle on medicinal powders restraining blood, such as chamomile and dragon’s blood and incense, and similar things; then keep its parts exposed for an hour, then put it in cold water; and when the bleeding stops, if it comes, let her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate seeds and rue seeds and similar things, and then take barley flour, and keep it down with honey and mustard, and make I apply it on her back
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stops, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	And if that does not happen, if it makes wind at the back and has swellings like wounds; then take lint, and soak it in the juice of plantain or in the juice of aglentier with old wine, and make wind at the sore.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess rests, if the wound is cleansed until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and is like a black head, as I have said before; and then heal the wound until it is healed
des apostemes de la marris	Emoroids are openings of veins which without support are not usually accompanied; and when they are old they become tough; and we have said concerning the signs and symptoms, I will now say those which relate to their cure. I say that emoroids and toughened skin, when they are pricked in the marrow, and they are not felt, if only they are treated by fire. Those which are at the entrance of the marrow, we can feel, and we can cure them. It is therefore necessary that you place the woman in a cold house, then extend the nail as it were a staple, grasp it at its root, then sprinkle on medicines which restrain blood, such as acacia and dragon’s blood and incense, and similar things; then withdraw the needle an hour later, and put it in cold water; and if there is still bleeding, if she sits in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate seeds and fennel and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and vinegar, and make one application on her back. And if it stops, that is good. If not, make her breathe vinegar at her back and have her drink vinegar mixed with wine vinegar, and make her breathe again. And when the abscess is healed, if the wound is still bleeding, it should be sutured until it is healed; and that which is called the “albathir” is red, and is like a rough chief, if you cover it as I have said the toughened skin; and then it should be sutured until it is healed. And when the abscess is healed, if the wound is still bleeding, it should be sutured until it is healed; and that which is called the “albathir” is red, and is like a rough chief, if you cover it as I have said the toughened skin; and then it should be sutured until it is healed.
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	There are many kinds of abscesses that come in the belly, such as carbuncles and perforated abscesses and herpes and piles and fistulas and hemorrhoids and scalded abscesses, and other diseases that I have mentioned in the division
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is necessary that I say that I die in this treatment of the burn which comes in the marrow, which is not a burn but only boils; and if you see the work of fire, look if the burn is still in its beginning, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red when you see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore do not hasten me to pierce [the burn], but let me measure until the pain is eased; and then seat the patient on a chair, and give him two small chairs or he will recline, and support him on his back and join his limbs as they are turned away from the limb; and let his thighs be spread out, and put his arms across his knees, and bind them well with a bandage; and then pour the bail towards the breast bone, and bring the instrument from which we expel the pus from the marrow, so that this form comes; and know that when you bring this instrument, that you must first feel the depth of the marrow, so that what enters with the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not damage the patient; and if the instrument is large, if you must cover the depth of the marrow with a cloth, so that the instrument does not hurt; and know that you must put the horn of the instrument under, and that you must hold the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess bursts, and we put a hand over the head, if it covers the head and shoulder joint; and when the wound is emptied, if you put into the wound some soft substances in rose oil or dry green oil; put the dressing firmly over the wound, and put over the wound and the surrounding area a clean cloth soaked in water or mallow which have been boiled; then cure after two days following this, until it is healed; and never lift the wound and the dressing by clinking with water and honey, and then with water or licorice root and alum which have been boiled; then return to the oiling.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is closed in the wound, if you must beware of cooking iron, but cure it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	From infancy.
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	The master first of all must know the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs are when you see the woman pressing down with her mouth, and longing to smell out the head: then the child hastens to issue forth; and when the child’s head is according to the natural figure, and comes out whole, and is seconded by him; and when you see these signs, if you must press gently on her belly, so that the child comes out stretched; for when he descends upon his head, if he is seconded by him, and the child is born whole, he will deliver his superfluities by natural means.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it never comes from his feet, or comes from the ribs or arms, or from his belly, or even from his head, and is converted by chance from his collar, and by other wicked figures; if the master is at the dance that she be wise and discreet in these things, and she must beware of error and deceit, and I will show you all the figures in which we must help her
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes down naturally on its navel, and the woman gives birth, and the afterbirth is weak, let her sit on a seat, or the women hold her; and arise its nature of oil or rue or rue oil or any fat, and then she will deliver between her two thighs the small sac that is its form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	And open the second vein, and bind it to its nail as long as the moisture that is in the core escapes; and press the belly of the woman as long as the fetus descends, and if it does not descend, if you suspect, clench the woman with the muscle of fenugrec with oil of sesame; then make her drink and vomit violently, and keep her mouth and nose covered for an hour: if the fetus is gone now.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands come out violently, if you suspect, that you must hold them lightly loose; and if they do not enter, put the woman upon a chair, and support her feet high; then withdraw the chair from the ground, and hold her, that she does not cough; and if the hands still do not enter, and the fetus is dead, if you bind the hands at the shoulder which is in front, and pull out the fetus, and soothe equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	From the birth of the child upon his feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes upon his feet, if one can push up; and then twist back and forth, until they are even; then take hold of the feet and stretch back and forth.</start_of_turn>
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If he leaps up to his buttocks, if the master commands him to grab, and makes him vomit with disgust; if he leaps further, God help him.</start_of_turn
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	If not so fierce as we have said, if the limb hangs by a thread and hangs by a thread, as long as it remains according to its natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For in such a case it is easily done.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if he does not leap so far as we have said, say if he takes muscle from the height, oil of alum, gum masticated, and broth; and put on the nature of the woman inside and drive out this nausea, then make her sit in hot water until the ribs are soft; and when she is softened from the ribs, give her a collar of myrrh, and put on her clothes, and leave her for an hour; then make her sit on her seat, and make her vomit and strain her mouth and her nose, and take her pulse slightly, for the child now leaps.</start_of_turn
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	because of the child’s discharge from his genitals.
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, if he puts his hands on his face and his head hangs down; either he is overcome with sleep on his neck, and his tongue hangs out; or he is overcome with fear and cries out; he folds his hands on his face and his hands, and then grasps his hands over his belly, and pulls his cushions downwards, until they are visible from his throat; and if the child does not jump, take his hands and move them, then move his belly upwards, and let go of his hands; and the child will clap his hands and clap. Command the woman to stay calm until the child is gone.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	And so the child cries and cries; and instructs the woman to stay close until the children are gone.
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	I can teach you how to reposition the limb: if you are unable to reposition it, if you make the woman rise up, call for help; if she is unable to call for help, make her sit on her lap, and pull the legs forward; then join the limb that I have mentioned. If she does not improve, make her sit on a chair, then observe to reposition the limb; and when the child recovers his natural position, make her spit out, and command her to stay calm until the child is gone.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	From the birth of the child on his neck, and he has spread out his hands, and his face turned towards his mother's back.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	I command that you grasp her hand firmly, then turn it back and forth; and when it is straightened, apply the viscous substance of alum and oil, as we have said before; and then I command her that she move back and forth; and when you have done this, make her sit in her usual place and command her to rest; and make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	From this manner, at all times in the secondine.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement. de l’issue des gemelz	When the head of the shoulder is slightly displaced.
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	The head of the shoulder dislocates often, but never without some movement of the limb; and this is not a strange thing, and often happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	What is strained and does not live, if its name be known; I know that, for they are multiplied, and are devoured by the bile which is bound to the spleen; and never does it go out as naturally as all the rest, as we have said.

If it goes out groaning, as we have said, and the cure be like this, and be the subtle dance, and make haste and lightly what it makes; and do thus as it be worth doing for the health of others.
de plusors enfans	Furthermore.

Never are they formed in the marrow I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more than XV, and they are all formed like children by the measure of their glorious age, and it is right that the glorious dance should take all this, for by chance many things happen; do as it is right
de l’enfant mort	Of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you cure the woman of a dead child or womb, if as I have said in the division, and she does not come into labor, and you are constrained by the work of your hands; if you believe that the woman is of sound health and has no accident or fears of death; if you believe that the woman is relaxed on her back, and her shoulders relaxed, arms raised, and legs lifted; and that the ministering hand grasps two fingers, or lies bound if she is not to be treated with the descending of the child; then smear the mouth of the woman with soft oil infused with mustard, alum, and flaxseed and poppy seed; then anoint her hands with these oils and these unguents; then put them into the belly lightly, then ask her to lie down or she may push out the sponges that are convenient for this; take warning if the child appears to descend upon her head; if she tears the sponges in her eyes or nose or mouth or in the corners of her eyes or on her beard or in her teeth or near her ribs, and the descending is upon pieces, she tears or squints and has low ribs; and it is necessary that she grasp the sponge with her right hand, and put the elbow between her two fingers of her left hand, and hold it firmly with her whole left hand, and insert the sponge into none of the places that we have said, until it comes to the thing that is empty; and that is the form of the sponge.
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then the pincer grasps another one, or the third if you are in haste, if the extraction is even; and then extend them evenly by moving from side to side, in order to stretch, and grasp the teeth firmly, as is the form.
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if some remains stuck, if one feels some of its two oils slipping, and holds them in that part, and treats the other part; and if it does not slip, if put the pincer on that part or even higher up, and make it so until it comes loose entirely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes in front of the other, and it cannot be pulled back by the stretching, then it must be that you wrap around the drapeil, until it is whole; then pull towards the joint of the thumb or the wrist, and it must be that you do the same with the other hand, and make two fingers
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	If the head of the shoulder is large and is twisted out of joint, or if there is a collection of blood clots assembled, if you must stretch the spinous process between your thumbs and grasp the head and draw out the clot; or you must roll it with the instrument called "almidach," which is similar to the instruments or chapter following this one; and in the middle make the limb naturally swell outwards; and then treat the bones as if they were tough, and if the shoulder joint is forced out, it will strain at the forcele, whether it is fractured or not, until the moisture that is either issuing or remaining comes out; and if it cannot issue, if the bone breaks into pieces at the root that you must break; and if it is embedded in the belly or along the ribs, if you must pierce as much as the moisture comes out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the swelling is on its side, if the limb is drawn towards the mouth of the marrow is lighter.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is swollen on the belly or the side, it is proper that you should drain it with a drape enveloped over the hand; and stretch the belly or the side, until the moisture which is in it is gone. And if another limb is stiff, and the head of the shoulder is dislocated, if the hand is clasped by the wrist, and you pull it out to the mouth of the wrist; then there is one or two incisions, and you pull out forcefully. And if the mouth of the wrist is retracted by the surrounding fat, if you cannot pass it through, you must bring about moisture and fat things; and you must apply poultices, and soak in soft and moistening water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the fetus is on the cost, and you put it even, if you bring about what we have said of the living child; and if there is no progress, if you must pull out by pieces, and leave nothing of the afterbirth.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	When you have done this, if anything mentioned above comes to pass in the belly; and if blood comes from an opening, if there be any restraining liquid put in, and other cures are added.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose belly had two infants, and she had put one out and was consoling the other.

je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I went to call for help, and I thought for a long time, and I could not soothe the wound.</start_of_turn
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on strong dressing, and there came out a bone, and after that another day.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marvel at the mouth, for this belly has no bone.

I wish the wound, and in clumsy hands, as long as the woman remained in pain; and I saw the woman long tense with fear; and this was enough for me in this chapter except for what happened that when the master found an unusual thing, he had to ask for help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	when he had to reset the dislocation.
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Then comes the form of pressure, as we find in books; and at this point there are two tears in two limbs.

However, the corners of the restriction must be more subtle than restrictive; and make of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the vessel must be closed or wide open; and the edge of the tree must be grasped, and long one palm and a half; and in between the two limbs there must be two needles of the same measure, which are fixed one against the other, half palm long or more; and these two needles are held in the mouth of the belly to open when the two corners are turned
