Another form, more subtle and lighter, is made of ebony or boxwood, according to the shape of the nails; and it has two handles two inches long, and two inches wide; and when you see the surgeon open the mouth of the instrument, sit the woman beside me, hold the pieces firmly and extend the legs over, then place the two handles together in the mouth of the instrument, and hold the head of the instrument between her thighs; then grasp your hand over the instrument, as if you had made the nails even, according to the quantity that you see the surgeon open the mouth of the instrument, until the bowl makes the sound it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all very strong, and their numbers multiply their semblance; and when you see them appear, the work is done more quickly, and the more numerous they are, the higher are their homes for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not desire the instrument until it has appeared, because its necessity is not negligible.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the second stage is retained in infancy, if you command the patient to hold her breath, and then make her spit out phlegm, and strain your hands at the mouth and nose; and if she spits out for that, it is well done
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take I pot, and make I hole or cut, and I put herbes in it that can open the mouth of the mare, as with calamine, rue, anis, camomile, cassia and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, are cooked or boiled in water over the fire; then put a caine or hole in the pot, and the other head in the mare's mouth, and hold it tight until the vapor comes from inside the mare; then make her sneeze as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second joint is grasped violently.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if she remains after this treatment, and there is no other remedy, as I command at the dance that she moisten her left hand with oil of sesame or in almond paste, and then put it back in its place, and command her the second time; and when she has found it, if you grasp and extend both thumbs forward and backward, so that the mare does not bite at the extraction; but it is commanded to move gently forward and backward, and then treat her. If she comes and is relieved of the pain.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	If the mouth of the marrow is swollen, we have said the cure is to perform a purgation and fumigate with herbs; and if it is not of all that we have said, if you hesitate to do it, do not use it; but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the marrow be bound to the hip of the woman, then to close with oil of marigold. If you do this and restore her, force will come; but nevertheless, when she is forced, if there comes a bad odor from the stomach and head, and vomiting, it will harm the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If it is suspected that the fumigations are suitable for this case: neither of the former has proved fumigation with rue herbs and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument in which we fumigate the woman at the retention of the flowers and the secondine if it is thus:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	It is like a dog that barks; put the beard under the fire; and either make fumigations over the charcoal and burn it until it is consumed, and start another.
de percier lou fondement	To pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have the sense of the foundation, and thus they are stifled by a subtle sickness: if you wish to cure it, you must cut off that which causes it at its root, and do not prick at the spleen with an acute spur, and keep the dressing so that it does not touch; then put on soft linen soaked in wine and oil, and cure with oil until it is healed
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	If you doubt that it will not stay in place, if you put or remove a weight of lead, and you leave the hands motionless, and be still as when the boy saw the hare in the chamber.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	Under no circumstances does this stupid fellow come to the rescue of a wound or an abscess; if you must cover this up, if either it be cured or as we have said, with a weight of lead.</start_of_turn>
de la fistule dou fondement	from the foundation of the fistula
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistules coming from below the foundation are nodulation, and those that come from above the foundation deflect, or in the space of two parts, if there is one fistula or more; and when the nodulation is ancient, if it is on the back, and there is moisture or white bile, and never are these fistulas permanent; and they are known by the patient when they pass or evacuate something, and by chance in a jump.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	If there are fistulas that reach the bladder, and halfway up the thigh; and reach up to the hip joint, and up to the navel.</start_of_turn>
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus it is known that the fistula that comes from the foundation is not permanent; and that when you bite your thumb or the foundation, and insert a thin needle or iron awl into the fistula when there is no pain.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is pain, if you insert a little sponge or a horsehair, as long as you feel the pain or the swelling at your thumb; and if you do not feel it, and there is no vomiting or evacuation, no diarrhea or wind, as we have said: it is useless; if you are in a hurry to cure it.</start_of_turn>
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula persists until the bladder or the urine duct, if in a jump the urine escapes and cannot be retained by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it be pierced up to the hip joint, if it is the vein that is coming up to the root; if there is no twisting and the sign of pain is not present, if it is only swollen, and no medicine or support by oil is of any use; in such fistulas there is no remedy save labor, and the folly of fools who interfere with it.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In that one which is neither new nor old, there is hope of recovery by fire, as I have experienced; and that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and you extend the legs until they reach the knees, and incline the knees towards his belly; then make a trial of pulling, or of pressing if there is twisting, until you feel pain or the trial comes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels pain at the root of the finger, if you command him to bite his thumb, if he senses that he has indeed perceived it; or if it is uncovered or if you feel between his thumb and index finger the flesh or nail, then extract the foreign object which is causing the pain; if not, it will not heal.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	We cannot treat all ailments well, but this is often the case; and we must help in this way. If we burn the cautery superficially according to the size of the fistula, as it has been said; and we pack all around in the fistula, until it comes out from the root; and do this two or three times, until you see that these hairs that must be cauterized are burned, which are similar to a bundle of hair; and then we treat with moist compresses covering the wound, until the hair has healed, and then we treat with oil that binds the hair and closes the wound.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is still sane, that is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If he is still sane, that is good; but if he attempts it and does not pierce until he reaches the root, and between his thumb and the attempt put on a thick covering of hair or wool, and you will see the fistula at the place where it lies under the covering; if you cut off the beginning of the fistula, and hold it fast before the attempt, and burn the cautery afterwards, until it reaches the top of the attempt; and the attempt will be delivered, and will be cured. Then remove the hair or wool that seemed like a sparrow’s quill, and there will be nothing left.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	If he does not go away of himself, and stands between you and the work, let the fire cautery or the medicine suffice.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery, two things are assembled: namely, the burning of these hairs that grow, and the extraction of blood and the drying of moisture; then the treatment of soft swellings by burying or chopping them, until the body sweats; and from there the burnt hair is cured. Then cure the wound of the abscess with dry charcoal, and these are the dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, if it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	When the fistula comes up to the surface of the skin and is loosened from its root, if the thumb or the foundation is grasped or displaced, inquire about that.</start_of_turn>
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If thou feel the attempt, and between two is the thread or the flesh or bone, or it is almost certain to pierce, if there be no other way but to leave it and hope, by the administration of one of these three methods: either thou cauterize it as we have said, or thou draw it out whole, or if thou wouldst do so, put in attempts and cure as first; and do not go too deep, for thou wilt cover only the tenement that holds the foundation, and bring out the discharge in the natural way; then cure it as we have said; by chance if it be well, or thou expel that covering and the mucus then when it is cut off from the foundation, or by attempt or by other pointed instrument; then bind up that wound which is in the wound, as thou wouldst; then study to restore the wound, and to stop the fistula in the posterior part of the foundation: if it be a lighter thing to the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And never are fistulas like this: when you bite the attempt in the fistula, and it is either costs or touches the underside of the skin at the root, if you take a bite pierced at the head like this.
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And there is always a thread taut in two, and the attempt is to the end of the fistula as long as it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	And if it is pierced at the root of the foundation, then draw out the thread of that which is pierced, so that you bite your head or the root; and pull the thread of the head, and unite the two ends together, and constrain one to the other, and leave it for one or two; and do not restrain at any time, until the thread has overcome these hurdles that are between two things, and that are pricked; then cure the wound until it is healed and healthy.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not burst, if you force it to burst in all the ways you can, it will not be too much harm.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not befitting me to make it burst with force, and then cure it, as we have said, until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spiny bladder from which the fistula is made is smooth on one part and rough on the other; and because of this we do not touch this with that which we must not touch, as you see here.
des emorroydes	Des emorroydes
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racine; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you wish to keep the suture according to this method: take one thread and pierce it through a needle, then pass the thread through from below and pierce the needle through from the other side; then draw up two threads from the needle, and if it is thick; restrain the thread firmly, then knot the thread and withdraw the needle, and do the same with all the others, and leave one to correct the excess blood; then put on the foundation a soaked bandage in rose oil or cerate, and put on the foundation, and command the patient to rest; and then leave it until it bleeds, and when it is bled out, if the wound is cleansed and other treatments have been given, until it is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	Then leave it until it quiets down, and when it has quieted, if the treatment for swelling and other treatments are complete, while he is still sane.</start_of_turn>
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	There are often spasms of the bowels due to a constriction of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine is of no avail.</start_of_turn
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you notice swelling at the root of a nail or at the nail itself, which does not allow it to dry; then treat it until it is healed if possible; and if it does not heal, if you must repeat the scraping more vigorously than before, until it bleeds, and be scraped off; then treat it until it is healed
dou fremit	But let him rest.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Formice is a small outgrowth that is planted before the limb, and goes out to the end like a claw; and never does the trueve touch it, and one feels it as if dead from fear, and comes on the whole limb, and more than in any other part.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure for this is that you take a sliver of goose feather, or a sliver of strong vulture, and put that sliver on the wound, until it circles the wound all around; then stretch your hand at full length until you grasp the wound all around, and put it out to the end, and scrape the wound from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see it, if you do this with a needle or iron according to this shape, and be discreet and patient below:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	And if you see it, if you do this with a needle or iron according to this shape, and be discreet and patient below, do not perceive, for it must hold still, and press and if you see it, if you cauterize the edge, as it is before or the master of cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	and be discreet and patient below, do not perceive, for it must hold still, and press and if you see it, if you cauterize the edge, as it is before or the master of cautery.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	and be discreet and patient below, do not perceive, for it must hold still, and press and if you see it, if you cauterize the edge, as it is before or the master of cautery.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those who are feeble and painful in the treatment of children are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	Their form is small and large if it is very wide, or the belly is bound in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And if there is a swelling or the belly is bound, if you see, and the shoulder is either pulled or pierced; and if there are two holes in one rib and one in the other; or if the belly or the abdomen has been given medicines from a bladder of best or parchment, or if it has been pierced all around with fine holes, and there is between each hole one must of space, then put in these holes one strong thread of thread like a cross or in a circle; and assemble the belly like a chive; and when the medicine is inside, if there is an instrument before a strong thread, then clip it; and that is the shape of a circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine neither be too hot nor too cold; anoint the head with ointment of oil or balm of egg, or something similar; then bind it lightly; then grasp the physician by both hands together, until it is quite visible; then remove the ointment, and leave the patient his legs uncovered, and if the medicine sees that it is sufficient, if the swelling has diminished; and if he sleeps through the night, it is more effective.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you see him listless in a state of vomiting of the belly, and the medicine hastens to depart, if he persists as long as he is well.</start_of_turn>
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if there is bruising or swelling, or abscess, if the ointment is as soft as for a young child; and this is the form of the soft ointment that is placed on the skin without straining it:
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already mentioned in the previous section the treatment of wounds; or rather, the treatment of hands and medicines, as appropriate.</start_of_turn>
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse depending on how they are made, and depending on the nature of the wound or the part that is wounded, and from how they are made.</start_of_turn
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things that are done for wounds are done by the bite of a stone, and the size of a spear or nail, or an arrow or staff or saw, or similar things; or that are done according to the laws of nature, as for wounds that bleed on the neck, or on the head, or the arm, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure for a wound of the head and I will begin with simple wounds, for the memory will come back in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes or a fracture occurs, and the bone is not broken, if you take care that it is not from a stone wound or other similar things, and the skin is thoroughly ruptured and the wound is large, you doubt the stitching of the wound: if you do this too soon after the wound, the head of the fracture will heal in vain, even if there is blood in the wound; or if the blood is on the contrary side of the wound. Listen carefully to the patient's swelling of wine and meat.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it does not heal, if either vomiting occurs or he does not drink wine, does not eat meat; and put out the wound, if there is pus coming out, cover the wound with moist lint with rose oil only, or with styptic wine; and if there is no need for stitching the wound, if it is fresh throughout its extent, and it is not moved by the air, dust, or anything else, I will tell you later; and if it has been moved, put on some ointments, until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	If the wound is large, like a saw cut and similar, and the edges do not reunite by themselves, if you reunite them with stitches, like when I say wounds on the belly, with stitches.</start_of_turn>
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed by the bone, and is raw, and cannot be held together by anything but a stitch, then cure the wound with medicine, and restore flesh in place of skin, and command the patient to eat coarse food, such as testicles and barley, as well as poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find or split skin that is not attached to the bone, if you can grasp it all at once, grasp firmly, then cure; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped by medicines, if the artery, and if you find it dislocated, if you tie it with a thread; and if that does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	If these wounds are small and simple, apply a light dressing: and if it has moved, place this powder that solidifies as quickly as it dries.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is this: take incense one part; dragon’s blood two parts; live charcoal three parts, and grind them finely, and apply to the wound, and press firmly, until it is well closed and joins together again; and then tie well and leave it undisturbed, if it does not swell; for we do not burn the medicine until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never do we make this charcoal alone, when we do not have incense or dragon's blood, but that the wound has not moved.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound has moved, even if it be so while it is still fresh, do not put on this plaster; but put on some unguents which digest, or poultices made of fine oatmeal and honey, until it has bled enough; then treat with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	If a fracture accompanies the wound, and it is small, if you grasp the wound with fine tweezers; I will tell you about fractures later.</start_of_turn>
de la plaie dou col	And I shall tell you afterwards about the bursting of the head wound
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	And I shall tell you afterwards about the bursting of the head wound. If there is no difference between it and the bursting of the head, but if the neck or the artery is cut
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is a nerve, if there is nothing else that can be done except to leave the wound alone, and do not put anything restraining, for it hinders the nerve and makes it shrink; do not put anything rough on the wound, for the substance of the nerve is cold, and its continuation is with the brain, which is the most important limb; but if the medicine is strong, like warm water with sweet oil, and honey mixed with rosemary oil, and cucumber washed in sweet water, and other stones of this kind, and moist unguents.</start_of_turn>
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is great, if the wound is closed with stitches, then the cure until it is healed
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	If wounds are deep and the flesh is swollen and full of blood, if the artery is severed, and blood flows freely; if the esophagus or the gullet is pierced, or the spleen, or the cauterize is mixed with blood; if the thorn of the throat is severed, or the cartilage, and the tongue is retained, because the meat will slip down; and then the wound must be strained out immediately, and left alone for some days, and then cured by gentle means until it is healed; and if the wound has made an imprint in the bone, if there are pieces of bone, if the fragments must be driven out, these things must not be done; let the wound rest until it has healed naturally.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is fistula, if the treatment is as I have said in the chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	Of a wound from a lance or a knife.
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it be a wound from a lance or a knife, and the wound is deep, look if there is a sign of air escaping from the wound: if so, that the wound is mortal; if not, and the wound is fresh throughout, do not put anything at the first hour but powder; do not bind it with the wound that it does not remain painful as it deepens, and remove it and comfort the patient; but put on a visible dressing, and bind it twice; if there is no visible dressing, put in the wound some cotton to absorb the moisture, and make the patient sleep over the wound for three days, or more; if there is no spasm, do not move or strain the body or limbs unnecessarily.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	The treatment of boils and other cures, as long as it is sane; and if it does not heal, and if it bursts, then that there is fistula; as it should be.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	If the wound is from a cut or a knife, and it is simple or at the front, if the treatment of what is before is sufficient; if it is large, with stitches; if it is small, with powder; if it is embedded in the bone, and has broken pieces, if you want to close the wound, and the edges are raw; but if they are not raw, leave the wound open, if it aligns with the extraction of the foreign body; and for other wounds, the judge will decide as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	And in other wounds as in other members, the judge shall determine as we have said.
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The breaking of the belly is great and medium and small; from a great wound no time the intestine, or no time the intestines, by which the introduction of food is hindered; and the costure is more painful, and no time is worth more than the small wound than the great, because it is more likely to point the intestines back in, if they are not pointed back immediately; for the intestines swell so much that they feel the fruit, if they go back in more points, and for this reason is better the lesser wound, for this reason it is better to leave the intestines in their place than to reintroduce them with other food. And the discharge from the belly is in three ways: the two common costures come in the costure of the belly, and the costure of the other wounds of the skin and two other costures are common with other wounds; and all of them are more appropriate with the costure of the belly, and I will say a mouthful and declare.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small and nothing from the intestines is pressing, and only a little pain exists, this can be remedied in two ways: either by the small size of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen by the fruit.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, soak the area in part with: moisten a sponge or I fold a cloth in warm water only, or you can soak in warm water that stings and bites and pierces, and raise the intestine until it swells to its bony size; and do not under any circumstances do anything that would restrain, for it is mute that awe must suffer in order to de-swell.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, if the intestine is moistened with water or raised and cooked badly, for in this way the entrance is aligned with the thing; and if it cannot enter, if there is a space, make a space for the wound at the instrument and press the swellings; and the first cure is mute that the size, that we must not cut without great necessity, and this is the instrument for cutting: if you cut inwards towards the curve and do not go out, and once this has been done, cut off:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is swollen, and the intestines are twisted, if you stop bleeding in accordance with its natural form in its place, know that this is useless, for it is of no avail.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the lower part of the belly, if you command the patient to sit up on his back and raise his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the lower part of the belly, put the head and the heel higher than the lower parts, and if the belly is twisted to the right or left side, put your hand in such a way that the higher part be above the lower part; and then you must support what I have said in great and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	In small wounds, put between your hands the ministering oil that holds all the surrounding parts together; and gather the layers.  This is the common method of stitching, and take a needle or several, according to the quantity of the wound, then leave some space around the head of the wound, and pierce the two holes of the skin with the two holes of the needle, which is below the skin, until you have pierced through to that part, and gather the two heads of the needle together with three threads.  Then strain a double thread around the needle at two parts, and gather the two ends of the wound together, and then leave some space, and pierce another needle; then tie the thread as you did for the first needle, and do not cease doing so until all the wound is held together; and let the needles be moderate, between fine and coarse, for fine needles hold all the substance, and the too coarse if they do not penetrate well: for this reason they should be moderate.  Do not force the needles too far from the substance and the skin, that they do not hold and open the wound before the suture; and then close the holes of the needles, that they do not hurt the patient at night, and put patches or bandages over the holes of the needles to hold, and leave them until the wound is healed; and this method of stitching with needles is more convenient in small wounds, for there is only need for one needle or two for the second stitching, and that you gather the two holes of the skin and the two holes of the needle together with a needle or there is one strong thread in the middle.  And when you have pierced through these two holes together, remember the needle at the part or where you began, in the manner in which we cut the threads; and leave some space between each stitch the thickness of a small fist.  This stitching is enough for the layman, and I stitched a wound once like this, which was swollen from a knife, and the wound was more than a palm of great, and there were intestines very two palms of great, and the wound was in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I will return the intestines when they have been gone for twenty-four hours, and the wound will be closed after fifteen days; the cure was successful, and he was healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	Then the physician saw that he was dying, and this was a miracle; and I did not treat him with any medicine, for I was in Italy where there was no physician, no medicine; and I did nothing more for the wound than to dress it twice a day with wool, and to bathe it in honey until it healed.</start_of_turn>
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or you will tell me two proper ways of stitching: take the needle, and pass it through the lower part until you reach the tip; when it has grasped the right edge of the wound, if you have pricked too deep or the needle has slipped, and you must pass the needle through from the other side of the wound until you reach the lower part; and you must understand this stitching as if you were sewing like a cobbler, and that you leave once the tip is on one side, and you take it back on the other, until the stitching is complete.</start_of_turn
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of stitching, which Galiens does with great skill, if it is done without any fault, joins the two parts together naturally and brings one of the chiefs close to the other chief, in this manner: pierce a needle or chief of the neighbouring area, and pierce only the lower part, and leave the two chiefs of the syfac; then withdraw the needle and pierce from the back outwards until the hole reaches the centre, leaving two chiefs of the syfac; then pierce the one and the other from the back outwards until the hole reaches the centre, making two further holes in the neighbouring area on the other side; and this is the most perfect method of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galiens says that this is an old tale, and no one testifies to it. We must suture the belly with two needles, or there must be thread in the hem. One needle must be pushed in from one side, and the other from the other side, in the manner of those who suture wounds; and it is better that when the turning point is in the middle of the belly, the stitching is finer than in other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judge of the wound is like the judge of other wounds: and that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, even if it has moved, if you stop the intestine and gut, then put on the dusting powder, and if it has moved, put on no dressing whatever it may be, until the wound has closed; and close the wound, and be sure of the suture, the dressing, and the dressing. Then cure the wound like the others, until it is healed. And if you have no medicine, if you put on only this, as soon as it begins to swell, cover it with wool, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	You need no other medicine for numerous affections than for simple wounds; and if you doubt that the wound will not commonly heal as principal members, you must cover it with fine linen soaked in warm olive oil, or in rose oil, and put it on the wound, and bandage the edges; and if it causes pain or putrefaction in the bowels, and happens frequently, if you bathe with black vinegar, and in the same way if the putrefaction comes up to the intestine; and if that is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small intestine.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines which are called "jeuns" cannot heal when they are swollen, for this is due to the swelling of the veins, and for the subtlety of the whole body, and for the proximity of their nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the flesh bursts from the wound, if it is returned backwards as the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is yellowed and becomes black, then you must know that you must tie the black part, that blood does not issue, for there are veins and arteries there; then close what is between the ribs, and suspend the two thumbs from the lower part of the wound until the burst is healed, and the wound will bow
de la routure dou boueil	because of moisture.</start_of_turn>
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is round, and the wound is small, if you can restore it in place among the ribs, because I have seen that one bone was swollen or pierced by a lance; and the wound was at the stomach and became filled and turned into an fistula, and in this there was vomiting and diarrhea; I treated it according to what I could, and I did not cease to soften it until it healed, and the wound closed
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	When I see it soldered, I doubt that the patient has no harm in his belly; and there is no sign of harm, but there is much good, food and drink; and they report that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it must be closed in parts. Take tweezers and grasp the edges of the wound, and when the tweezers have gone beyond the opening, if you put two fingers over the opening, if it tears its opening; then pull out the tweezers, and do the same with another finger as before until the wound is whole.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If it is burned in the intestine, and there is no discomfort to the patient, and it can be closed with a fine thread which is cut from the intestine itself, in parts: take the head of this thread of intestine which is quite free, and then join to this head one thread of linen which is twisted, and pass the thread through the needle, and close the intestine, and hold it in its place; and this manner of stitching is not fierce except as regards the way of tying and hoping; and if the wound is great and wide, just as it is in one of the greater intestines, if there is no other remedy, except for subtility.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or that it is in a cavity.</start_of_turn>
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Wounds or incisions, when they swell, if they are called universally 'fistula', and even when they are closed and bound.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	A fistula is according to the truth a nodulation that is firm and white, or one from which no pain is felt; and is as closely shut as the quill of a bird; neither completely shut nor yet open; sometimes almost, sometimes quite open; sometimes little, sometimes much; and I have already spoken of this in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no pus, is only by one of the seven causes: that is to say, by the smallness of the blood or the hardness of the flesh; or by its malice; or because there is hardness within, and upon the bones, that does not allow new pus to arise; or there is too much pus; or the blood vessels are hardened, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the treatment; or because corruption is rapid from pestilence; or because the property of the region is late in digestion and in health, and flees by nature; or there is a vein or bone. And I have already mentioned all these causes and their signs and treatments in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Or I must tell you the cure for fistula, which is made by the work of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Wounds that occur in all limbs due to corruption; for there are fistulas which arise from great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or the spleen, or intestines, or bladder, or certain bones, or the spine, or in any joint of the hands or feet; and if they arise from the primary part of the limb, and there are similar lesions.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	All fistulas of this kind are grievous and do not heal easily, except by laborious and ignorant methods; and if there is no fistula that does not rise to the surface except as I have said, and you have hope of a cure, and you see it grow, if it is straight, if the knot is loosed; and if it is twisted, if the hook of a needle attempt to plunge, for it will swell inward towards the twist; and if the fistula is through and through and you do not know how to bind it firmly, if it is split by one of the holes, for the moisture is so strong from one hole to another, and it softens; then when the hook is gently drawn away from the wound, you must know whether there is bone or nerve, and is chewed through by the infection, and ask the patient about the pain he feels at the touch of your hand, and the place where it is; and when you know truly the place or its distance from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery or vein, or from any of the things I have told you, if the wound agrees with what I have said, and the bone is exposed, and the corrupt parts that are within; and then the cure until it is healed, and if the fistula is deeply rooted from the outset, if you must expose the bone, as you must; then put in soft sutures in medicine, and stretch them up to the head of the fistula, until the medicine consumes the superfluous matter that remains at the bottom; and then put on greasy dressings to absorb the remaining discharge until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, if the cauterize as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, if it is exposed.

If you do not remove the foreign body at an opportune hour, if you place it upon the wound something that causes gangrene, and leave it until the flesh is rotten about the bones, then in this way you will have less pain in the bones; and if it is a large bone, such as a leg or thigh, you must only remove as much of the corruption as is necessary, leaving the bone whole; and then close the wound.  If there is a great part of the bone that is corrupt, and you bring it down to the marrow of the bone; if you cover it up and cover everything up to the corruption, and then cure it until it is healed; and I tell you of a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man about the age of thirty who had pain in his leg due to a cause that came from within the bone, until the matter came out of the leg, and there was no visible cause for opening; but he went mad with his folly and opened it so wide that it burst out, and it corrupted a great deal of matter and became a fistula, and there came out so much pus that it was filling the wound and moisture from the bone; and he remained treating it for two years, but there was no skill in his hands, as far as I remember, until I saw his leg and the medicines they were giving him, and what cured him of the bursting of the large bone; and it became red as blood and had the color of citrine.

I quickly bound one of these holes and saw through to the bone, which I found broken and bruised, and it continued to swell up to the marrow; I took out what appeared to be a fragment of bone, and I believed there was no further damage, except for that which I had already seen; and I began to apply soothing medicines for a long time, but I could not close the wound. Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The head of the shoulder is dislocated by moisture, by pressure, or by violence; and when you have remedied this corruption by the means of medicine, it profiteth you nothing, if you do not cover that limb until the corruption has passed, so that the patient escapes by this means from death, or from the greater malice of the defect of the limb; and the sign of this is that the limb becomes black, as though it were burnt by fire, and afterwards comes the blackness, for the corruption of the limb spreads throughout. de l’aposteme de l’ungle	De l’aposteme de l’ungle.
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that arises from the socket of the thumb, or the wrist, or by chance arises in other two places; and when it is inflamed, and one does not take care, if it comes there will be a running abscess that will burst and drain as much as it bursts the root of the thumb, and by chance it will burst all the way; and there comes the destruction up to the bone, so that there is great pain, and the head of the thumb is displaced, and the colour is dark brown.

des vils	Des vils.
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	The veins are large blood vessels enclosed in fatty matter full of black bile, which comes from many parts of the body. More comes from the legs of those who walk and work and carry burdens than from others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	And thus you must not give them any sudden expulsion of bile, but then the remainder of the balsam.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	There are two methods for treating wounds with fire: one is with sponges, and one is to cauterize the blood vessels.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The size is as follows: first, strongly heat the sharp limb until the great skin covering it is not tender, then strain the limb of the patient from under the buttock down to the heel; then cut the vein in one, two, or three places, of a large size, then close and burn out the black blood from the hand, from the tip to the wrist, until as much blood as the patient can endure has bled out; and then bind and command the patient to keep warm with meat covering the black bile; and repeat the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, without harming the patient.

The ailment of the limb is in this manner: open the limb of the patient, if there be hair, then put or bathe it in water, and raise the limb in warm water until it turns red, and swell the veins; and if you have no bath, if the fire burns, and then press the place where the vein is long at the elbow, or in the lower part at the ankle; then cover the leather with lint, and press the vein from the hip down, until it breaks when you feel it; and you will see it red and black, and when it comes out of the leather it seems like a white thread; then draw out the splinter, until it is freed from the leather, and then put on the lint lightly, and press again in another place; then press once more, or more if you must, and then put on the dressing, and press at the end of the bone, and hold until the second time; then draw out the splinter in order, until it is all out, and then press; and if you do not draw it out and lift it, if there be a thorn at all, and hold and draw, and there will be blood at the end, and turn your hand from one side to the other, until it is gone; and keep that it does not press, for if it presses, it will not be possible to draw or lift it, and comes to harm to the patient; and when you have finished treating it, take out the bone from the wound and cover it in wine and rose oil.
