des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	And never has this vein hands rained, neither when it opens at the elbow, or at the wrist, and there comes forth from the wound; cure it therefore as we have said before.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "buffalo disease", because it often causes swelling of the calves, and is a small vein that arises between skin and bone, and runs throughout the body upwards and downwards, and it is felt quite strongly from limb to limb, as long as it tears the skin or moves, and leaps forward; and it is accompanied by the discharge of various humors, such as blood, worms, and bile or fat. And there is doubt about its malice, for when it runs through the body, and it reaches the head, and comes out, by chance it returns, and destroys the fat; and this often happens.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it cured and treated, if it will not be cured until it goes away: if it is to be cured, then bind the limb above and below with a strong and firm bandage, then seize above and pull down, and if it does not yield, if you cauterize the fire above, until it dies; and the greatest nuisance it makes is when it comes into contact with oil, as we have said; and if you see it coming or near the oil, seize the eyebrow from below and pull down, then seize above, and pull down; and it is proper to have the patient take nourishment of nourishing foods for bad humors and to abstain from eating meat.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	When you see it cured and treated, if it will not be cured until it goes away: if it is to be cured, then bind the limb above and below with a strong and firm bandage, then seize above and pull down, and if it does not yield, if you cauterize the fire above, until it dies; and the greatest nuisance it makes is when it comes into contact with oil, as we have said; and if you see it coming or near the oil, seize the eyebrow from below and pull down, then seize above, and pull down; and it is proper to have the patient take nourishment of nourishing foods for bad humors and to abstain from eating meat.

This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and is a pain that comes in the limbs, and since it moves from limb to limb; and I saw this which I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I saw a woman who was sick, and found her arm limp, and saw a small swelling in the belly of the arm; and afterwards, I saw it rise up like a worm on the shoulder, more swollen than anything, as if there were silver coins when it burst from the limb, and spread to the shoulder, and then afterwards corrected throughout the limb, until it came to the other arm; then she told me that it would twist back into place again as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marvel at how she moves limb against limb, for I have never seen such a disease according to this method.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues. When you see the cure for this ailment, and the patient feels the pain, if the pain intensifies as we have said, and if the swelling above and below has increased, then take hold of the limb as tightly as the constraint of the swelling will allow; cauterize the limb; and if you do not see it moving at your eyes, if the cure has expelled the swelling, as with foul pills and serpin pills, and similar things.
des saiettes	When you see the cure for this ailment, and the patient feels the pain, if the pain intensifies as we have said, and if the swelling above and below has increased, then take hold of the limb as tightly as the constraint of the swelling will allow; cauterize the limb; and if you do not see it moving at your eyes, if the cure has expelled the swelling, as with foul pills and serpin pills, and similar things.
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Sponges are diverse, according to their appearance and according to the parts of the body where they are used.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The variety of wounds is such that some have large points, small, sharp, and blunt; and some have two angles, and some have tongues, and some have pieces; and that which tears in no limb tears in two ways: either in the principle limb, as the skull, forearm, elbow, shoulder, hip, knee, intestine, bladder, and similar limbs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When she cries out in any part of these limbs, and a sign of death, know this well, that I shall tell you afterwards: if you consider sparing the extraction of this arrow, for many deaths will follow; and when such a bad sign appears, do not spare the arrow, but extract it, and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the skull when the arrow cries out and pierces the bone, and leaps the blood that is above the skull, is like a scourging, swelling, and twisting of the bowels, and redness of the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and mixture of senses, and vomiting of bile; and by chance it is without nose or ear; or by chance it loses speech and voice; and leaps from the wound white moistor resembling blisters, and in leaping also like blood of the color of barley; and if this sign tells you, if you stay with the cure, extract the arrow if it is not already out.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	When the elbow strikes or breaks, the signs are that it is close to the left breast, and feels as though it were caught in something hard, not without pain; and by chance the elbow changes like a poul, with dark blood and comes with cold sweat and fainting: her life hangs in the balance with doubt that she will survive.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the fracture that never leaves without pain is that the wound swells, the throat is inflamed, the patient turns pale, and breathing is difficult and gasping for air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	If the splinter breaks in the palm of the hand, if it is removed with small nails; it causes great pain and swelling and breathing difficulty; and all the limb is stiff.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	If the splinter breaks or is in the stomach, by chance if it comes out without any indigestible meat of the body.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	If the splinter breaks or is in the stomach, and by chance comes out without any stool from the intestine, if there is no hope for the cure, do not attempt to extract the splinter.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	If the splinter breaks in the bladder, and the urine comes out in spurts and comes out with difficulty, and the patient feels great pain: the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, if it be made and the collarbone and the throat and the shoulder and the elbow and the wrist and the forearm and the hand, and the like of them, are all subject to various positions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the tendon is in the nerve or the artery, and it is not venomous, as I have said before, because of this I have seen that you do other things.</start_of_turn>
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	In my house there was a woman who swallowed a hairpin or piece of glass at the root of her ear: I grabbed her, and it slipped from the other side of the ear and she was cured without any damage.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And in a game there was a hairpin that she swallowed in the oil of the ear from the papere of the ear, and the hairpin was returned, and did not reach anything but the tip towards the face; and the hairpin was as big as a Turkish arch, at all this was heard without any damage.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And take out an arrow from the throat of a Christian; the arrow was Arabic with an ear: I grasped the bristles and pulled it out as much as I could, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And pulled out an arrow from the belly, which was hanging or swollen, and thought it was dying; and when it had not passed for thirty days, if it did not change; I cut on the arrow, squeezed it, and pulled it out, and there was no mishap.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if anyone has an arrow wound in the chest or back, and it is deep; and if the arrow remains in, and does not change its natural position, and does not cause pain in any of its natural works
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And if anyone has an arrow wound in his face, and it is deep; and if the arrow remains in, it causes great pain; and many others suffer in the same way
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And bring forth an arrow at home of the prince the king, that it was stuck in mud, and there was a decrease at the distant part; and the arrow was entirely recovered. I came to the cure after that it had been stuck for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I find the wound very sore.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I would have to do it with all my might, and I do not feel it; and there is no sensation of sharpness or pain on the distant ear
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the point of the arrow. I put on the chest a plaster that digests easily, so that the wound would not swell; and I saw the wound of the arrow come out
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put on the plaster for a few days, and then I removed the wound, and I left the patient long enough until he felt the arrow was still in his flesh; and he confessed to me
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I apply the corrosive medicine to the wound by hand every day until it is healed; and I try to remove it, and I feel the head of the splinter that is escaping from the wound; then I close the wound with the medicine, as long as the head of the splinter is visible; and it has healed well in two months, and then it grew so large that I was unable to bind it; so I continued to change it and bind it from one side and the other, and I could not stop it; therefore I had to endure the itching and suffering in many ways, until I finally took it out as it was well made, as it is mentioned at the end of this chapter, until I finished treating it, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the doctors say that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I restored it anyway, and the wound healed, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or tell me of the quality of the extraction of these arrows, for if you put your cure on that which I do not tell you, for the books do not teach me all that; but you know that masters know well enough about great things, and about that which is present and lacking, find nine works, and a new instrument, according as the things which arise in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that the arrows do not pierce flesh or are hooked, for there are two ways: either by the blood vessel or they enter, or by some other means; and that which leaps forth by the heel or enters, is an arrow that has penetrated flesh, and leaps no more ever.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not leap now, if you leave it until the marrow is carried round, and the swelling is lessened; and if it is hooked in the bone, and it cannot slip, if you leave it there for some days, and it moves little by little; and then it leaps, and if it does not leap, if it pierces round about everything that is soft, until the marrow is swollen, and then you draw it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the splinter is fixed in the bone of the cheek, and goes up to one of the ventricles of the brain, and there are no other symptoms that I have mentioned to the patient: do not remove it, but leave it until it is even again after some days, for if the splinter comes up to the surface, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the splinter is only fixed in the bone alone, and goes up only to the surface, and the patient suffers no other mishap, if the inflammation compels him to remove it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is firmly fixed and cannot be moved, if you administer tarres around it as I have said; then cure the limb once it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the splinter is embedded in the bone so that it cannot be seen, if there is any doubt; and if you see it, if you remove it without any instrument, and if you do not take sufficient care of the wound, and of the depth of the splinter, and there is no bone, nerve or vein, if the pain persists as long as the wound is large; then remove the splinter if you must. And if there is an ear attached to the splinter, hold it so that it holds together when you remove the bone that is connected to two parts of the muscle that you must remove, and then break or crush the ears of the splinter as much as you can, until you can remove it; and take care that you do not break the splinter, that you remove it more firmly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you do not grasp it at once, if the splinter remains fixed in the wound, grasp it firmly, for its extraction will bring relief.</start_of_turn>
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	If blood escapes because of the wound, do not oppose it; do as we have said in this chapter concerning the treatment. Guard the incision of the vein and the belly, and put in place whatever you wish to remove the arrow safely, whether it is by pulling, twisting, or closing tightly or loosely; put the patient in the position in which he was when the arrow went in, because it is the greatest help. If you do not know how, follow what the signs tell you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another place, or if there is no wound, or the skin is swollen in that place where it is seen or felt: then make the opening as wide as possible, as long as the tweezers can grasp; then remove it immediately.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it [the dislocation] is held in the bone, if you round your hand around the bone until it enters the bone, expand the bone, then draw it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot be grasped, if you leave it in place, and then resume the extraction until it comes out; if there is a lot of blood, if the limb has all the blood; and if it is chipped, and you see blood streaming profusely, if you give the instrument a slight curve, so that the tip of the arrow enters the curve of the instrument; and then pull out, and if the arrow is caught, if the instrument has a pointed handle entering, to ease the extraction
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	If the wound is surrounded, if you think the bone is fractured or the poison is in it, do not hesitate, then cure the wound as it should be cured.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If the wound is close to the bone or muscle or belly or bladder or ribs, and is adjacent, and you think it is necessary to cover it, do so; and hold the wound closed and the nerves, then extract the foreign body, and then suture the wound, if necessary; and cure it until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tweezers used to treat the splinters is like a bird's beak, and thus is this form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: great, moderate, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the wound at its edge is like the claw of a bird, to push out the point of the wound, as in this fashion:</start_of_turn
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the forceps to push and to grasp is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	From veins of common size.
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are veins that one must avoid, which are 16 in total: two veins that are behind the ears, which are near the cartilage; and two arteries that are in the two temples that appear; and two veins that are in the two armpits, which are called "aspirates"; and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is at the base of the nose; and the two veins that are on the chin; and the two veins that are under the tongue.</start_of_turn>
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The common veins of the arm are four in number: one is the cephalic, which runs alongside the left costal bone and is called the superficial vein; the second is the median, which is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins and is called the deep vein; the third is the basilic, which runs either on the left or right costal bone and is called the lateral vein; and the fourth is the abdominal, which lies above the navel and is the one from which blood is most commonly taken.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	The ulnar vein is between the radial and the ring, and if there are two veins in the forearm or leg, there are three veins: one which runs along the inside of the left costal bone, the second which is below the ankle on the right costal bone; and the third which is called the “pulse” and is in the ankle of the other leg. There are three veins in the other leg as well.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The blood of the veins that are behind the ears helps as old catharres and emigration; and the quality of the blood, as I have told you, is that you raise the head of the patient and wipe the hand or the veins are of a rough texture; then stretch the patient’s neck with a pin, as long as two veins open behind the ears in two loops dependent on the head: that is to say, if you see swelling there, then take the lancet and prick the vein until it reaches the bone, then keep your hand over the whole vein above, and press and the skin and the vein well two must pass through; and make the bleeding cease as long as you see; then strain and bind, as long as it is healed; and I have already said the incision and the cautery or first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The blood of the two arteries that are in the two temples, if it is like an ancient emigration, sode, and obtalmia accustomed, and at the root of the tears that are sharp, there are eyes; and the quality of the physician is like I have said: and that the patient has strained his neck, as the two veins open widely; and he feels the pulse of his thumb down to his wrist, and then he makes a sign of engagement; then he places his index finger on the vein in the upper part of his wrist, and he takes out the lancet down to the wrist, and then he takes hold of the vein in the upper part, and the clot, as he has done in two other veins, and he makes correction of the blood according to his need; then he frees the patient, and places his thumb on the vein for an hour, then he puts on a bandage; and then the swelling forms, and he leaves it until it is healed; and we have spoken of this in relation to its evacuation and its extraction, or its beginning in the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The blood from the front vein is worth as much as the blood from the cephalic vein, and has diseases of the old face, and a fistula, and redness; and if the patient turns his head violently, as the vein bursts. Then take the instrument called the "burr," which is like this:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	The blood from the front vein is worth as much as the blood from the cephalic vein, and has diseases of the old face, and a fistula, and redness; and if the patient turns his head violently, as the vein bursts. Then take the instrument called the "burr," which is like this. Put the point on the vein, and hold it with your hand, or something else, and let the blood flow as much as you see fit; then pull out the patient’s head, and tie the vein until it is healed and never again let the work be done with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not appropriate for me to say that the flame should be too thick; and the same with the other side, because the bone is close, and by chance the flame breaks the bone when it is subtle.</start_of_turn
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The blood from the two veins that are two fingers wide helps with the swelling, and the stiffness, and the redness, and the yellowing of the oil, and has diseases of the face; and the quality of its blood is that if the patient turns his head violently in any direction, as before; then do the same, and either let the blood flow freely, or let a long flame flow for a wide time, because there is no char.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is feeble, by chance if it breaks; then make an incision for the blood to escape, as much as you are able, and then bind it up tightly with a bandage, and press it firmly.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The blood of the vein does not rejoice if it is cold, and with fasting, and with diseases of the face, as with migraine and redness that comes to the face, and even when it is old; and the quality of the blood is that if the patient tightens his neck, then he tightens his jaw on his left hand, and takes a long flame and puts it in the space between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well enough in front, and without beginning to correct it now; and do not go too quickly, but correct the blood as you need, then leave it for a night, for it is much better restored; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The blood of the two armpits helps to remove swelling, and to begin mixing, and with many diseases, and with spasms, and with corrosions, and with herpes, and stomach ailments; and the quality of the blood is that if the patient tightens his neck from either side, as we have said; and let the master be standing above the patient’s head, and the patient sit on one seat, then close the vein long enough, and take out the blood gently, or as much as is necessary; then do the same in the other vein, then untie the thread, and gently tighten the veins in the middle, so that the patient is not strangled; and leave it until morning, so that the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	From the blood of the veins.
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The blood of the veins of the liver above helps to cause swelling in the mouth, corruption of the gums, ulcers of the liver, and vomiting and pain.</start_of_turn>
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	From the blood of the veins, if you wish to make the patient sit before you, and stretch his neck as I have said; then turn the vein, and look at the two veins, one on the right side of the vein and the other on the left side, and know them by their black colour, and by the fact that there are small black veins running alongside them: so join one and the other, and if you do not know them and you are in doubt, if you join the larger one from its head, and like wise do the two veins that are below and above, for this is a mean method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	From the blood below the tongue.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The blood of the veins below the tongue helps after the cephalic blood, and it is at the widening of the throat, and with eye diseases, and with mouth diseases; and the sign of health is if the patient sweats between his hands before the sun, and he holds the tongue, and look below at each cost side a black vein: join both of them, and do not press too hard, for below are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins that we commonly touch are often sound in two ways: either by puncturing with a sharp flame that burns broadly, or by olive oil if cut in trenches, and this is called 'anesil'; and they are large and oily according to the size and extent of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The flame that is made with a mirror is known as "mirtin", and is large as you see it:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And there must be a master to open the large veins filled with visible blood, and containing much blood and blood clots; and this is the form of the olive oil flame
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more pointed towards the tip, and is for healthier veins, or where there is thin blood.</start_of_turn>
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The blood of the basal vein, which is one of these veins, helps to cure ailments such as hoarseness, or swelling in the throat, or pain in the side, or in the belly; and it is beneficial that it flows smoothly and that it is separated from the artery that is beside it.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	If he grasps the root [of the hair] and blood flows, if he covers it, as I have said; and must not remain calm, but cut quickly as if on a whim.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	If the vein does not open visibly, if you must extract it, and tie another; or you wish no more blood, or you prefer to leave the vein closed in the arm: it will open visibly; and grasp the flame quickly, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	If you see that the blood vessel is moving, if you must extract the limb, touch the limb until you recognize the pulse; then mark the place, then bind the limb, grasp the vein with the flame quickly; and beware that you do not injure the artery when you see the limb swelling, for that is the artery: stop immediately.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you see blood spurt out like the urine of a child, and it is not red and bubbly, know that it is from an artery: haste then, and place your hand over the wound, then bind your hand tightly if it does not bleed; many times this has happened; if you leave the limb immobile, and do not move the patient, and remain calm, it will heal.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if it [the dislocation] is not held in place, and if you feel pain, and the physician is not present, if the artery bursts open because the head of the shoulder has retreated; grasp it without delay.</p>
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a bandage and bind it around the wound, take half and place it over the wound until the bleeding stops; if it does not stop, if necessary, use powders that will stop the bleeding; these styptics are not easily grasped in many situations due to the small size of the wound and the position of the limb.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The blood in the vein is aided by the support of the chest above and the neck below, because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said; and it is necessary for the health that the nerve which is below is not too constricted, and if it is too tight and the nerve is caught, it swells and the wound is closed, and by chance cannot heal; for this nerve is often torn, and if it is not torn in some people due to its delicacy, it is necessary to cauterize it with an instrument that is delicate.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a wound between the two nerves, if the pain lasts a long time.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The blood of the cephalic vein helps, as it draws blood from the head, and aids the eyes; and it is best to cauterize with the olive or mirtin flame, for it is the safest of all veins, as it has neither nerves nor arteries.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, it is necessary to inquire the matter more cautiously, and do not grieve if it does not succeed the first time, and we repeat; and by chance it swells the limb at some homes, which cannot be remedied the first time, but it does not grieve us
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is as you think.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about cautery is that it should only be performed when necessary to preserve health and avert future ailments; and that it should be done in one of the three veins which are either close or remote: namely, the cephalic, fasting, and basilar. It should be performed at the beginning of the prayer, during self-flagellation and during the after-meal prayers when the swelling appears; and it should be done immediately at the first yawn or after two or three yawns.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The blood which is administered for diseases has no fixed dose, but when necessary it is for girls or women up to seventy years old in all hours and at all tensions; and it is not permitted to give blood to children under twelve years of age, nor to women who are nursing for more than four months up to seven.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Must not be given to one who has passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when anyone feels sick, in whatever way, if it is allowed that he defends his intestines from a lesser hernia, if he has retained a fever, so that the veins do not draw out the intestines with the nourishing humors from the principal members; do not let him drink too much meat, nor too little, neither too much or too little of hydropics; and if he vomits after drinking wine, and suffering from a swelling of the belly, and multiple vomiting and diarrhea, and many women’s complaints, and childbirth, and watching, and lying down, and all his cares or discomforts; then subtilize the humors, if they are not large, by means of food and drink and medicine, if you have the power; then enter or bathe, so that nothing hinders the blood, and keep it warm for about a third, as we have said; and keep him engaged in work, and in guarding, and in luxury, and in other things; and bind his limbs and joints, and let the patient be higher than him whom we keep, and wipe his hands twice or thrice, and then remove the ligature gently from the middle, because if it is too tight or loose, it cannot be corrected without; and then wipe the body with the hands, until the veins swell and are felt; then moisten the patient with a little oil, then put his left hand over that vein below the elbow for a moment or two, until he feels the blood returning.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that run like strings to the healer, and if they are filled with windiness, so that when the flame is put on, it withdraws from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus is this; and if the vein is opened, the wound is too great, for in that case the healers must be warned in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	If the vein bleeds the first time, that is good; but if this does not happen, if it starts again for a second time, whether from the wound or from the patient’s condition, if the patient does not faint.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the limb is inflamed, and the patient hopes, and leaves it yellow or two, and does not bind the arm: by chance will come abscesses from this; do not enter or bathe, then restart the bleeding if it stops; and if it is slight, or without any apparent cause, and you doubt whether there will be less blood than you saw, if you are confident in that wound itself with all the flame directly; and do the work diligently, even if the limb is inflamed; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the limb inflamed, if you do not renew the blood flow, put on a bandage of oil, for it smoothens the hair of blood; and it makes the blood adhere to the limb where the oil is applied. And administer the oil bandage in small quantities so as to close the blood vessels, to stop the flow of blood; and this very thing brings about healing and swelling of the wound, when it is placed on the limb; if it is too subtle it escapes when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there comes a large abscess, which happens often, even if it is not dangerous except for this time or if the opening of the vein is small, if you are in a hurry, put on the limb a soft sponge soaked in water and a warm compress, and hold it in place for an hour; and it is likely that after the evacuation of blood from the vein, if it remains in the limb afterwards for several days, there will be no blackening or greening, unless it is due to something else. And if you see this, do not put anything else on it, such as aloes or myrrh diluted with calamine, mustard, or anything similar.</start_of_turn>
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there is swelling and appearance of blood in the basilisk: put your hand on it, and if you find the limb soft under the compression of your hand, if it is that kind of appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Leave then from this discourse whatever we have said, for by chance in court without an artery; but make.i. embalm it dry to harden the limb, then treat it with another remedy, until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	Treat each wound according to the quantity of its virtue, and the colour of the wound.</start_of_turn>
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if it is black without, if you leave it to fester as long as it is red; and if you see it large, if you leave it as long as it is subtle; and if it is too thick, if you leave it cool.</start_of_turn>
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is to be known to him who is plain and strong, and who has the mastery of bloodletting, that you must make the wound larger; and let the flame be large; and for him who is weak, do the contrary, and you must make him whole again and often, and you must make him whole by cutting across, not by pricking; and this method of bleeding is safer than the bleeding of a long duration which is large.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for him who has a cold body, it is to give soft bread soaked in pomegranate juice; if he is faint, give blood three or four times. And if he has a cold complexion, give before the blood soft bread soaked in honey or aromatic honey with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and fragrant honey.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if it smells of blood after the evacuation of blood, if it is likely that it has produced a clot of blood, and an odor of rotten eggs, and use other things that we have said in the division or chapter of syncope, for the evacuation of the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he sees blood again, and feels better another time, if it is suspected that it is caused by great bleeding, let him rest peacefully and quietly, according to the quantity of his continuous virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever saw his arm twisted after the first bleeding, and has stiffness, if he be well, should wait at least thirteen hours after the first bleeding, or after the twelfth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever saw himself cured on one side, if he must be cured on the other side, should wait until the next morning or the third hour.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is blood in the body which is already clotted, and causes fever; if it is likely to draw out a great quantity, and dilate the opening until it cries out in pieces; then that you reward all the conditions of blood, and put your hand over the pulse when it is well, so that the blood does not come out again in place of the pieces, and this often happens, when the patient is negligent; and do not do anything until you see it slip from the limb, and make the blood issue a second time, and the opening is closed, that you press firmly; if it is crooked, that you extend the limb urgently, because that would be bad; but leave it until it issues a second time; or you prick to the tip of the flame, until that which is frozen at the opening of the vein is forced out of the opening, and put on some oil and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein has fled, if you leave it and do not restrain it firmly, until the swelling is reduced.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessary is to drain blood the second time, if the same vein is still affected, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is white in place of the vein of the head because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And thus with the bleeding, if the patient grasps his hand in warm water, until the blood vessel is red; then bind it moderately, so that the wound opens well; then draw the hand through, neither wide nor long; or make a large opening and bring the blood vessel near to the wrist joint, and if it is not possible to withdraw it, grasp the hand in warm water and leave the blood clot in the water until enough has accumulated; and if this is done, do not reinsert the hand in warm water, for it is more harmful than beneficial in this case; and the blood of this vessel is more reliable than all other veins, for there is neither artery nor nerve in it.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The blood of the salivary vein of the right hand is worth for all the diseases of the liver, and this is the method: strain the hand and grasp it in warm water, until the vein is expelled; if it is seen. And if it is withdrawn, and if you manage to pull it out whole, do not grieve; and do not grasp too tightly, for the nerves are all stripped of hair. Then grasp the hand in warm water, if it is not frozen in the wound, and do not withdraw it.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as well as you can, if you put oil on the vein and bandage it securely, and do this for every wound.</start_of_turn>
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The blood in the left hand is worth for the disease of mice, and do the same as I have said concerning the other side.</start_of_turn
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The blood of the spleen is worth for all diseases that are caused by an excess of humors, as with diseases of the marrow, retention of flowers, diseases of the reins, and of the uterus and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of the blood is such that when the patient has too much pain in the belly and boils on the belly until it bursts, and lies under the joint of the belly; and if the belly is at the ankle, and from under the bone comes out mud of the reins; so must the spleen be great or somewhat large rain, or at the ankle, as much as the blood is worth.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you keep it healthy on the foot, if you guard against the nerves which are soft, and keep it sound like when you are grasping; and let the flame depart slowly.</start_of_turn>
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it cannot be moved, if you reset the limb in the water, and let the vein drain well.</start_of_turn>
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the patient must be bled for the first time, if he starts again from under a little bit, because the blood is salty; do not doubt, as we have said, and make the spleen of the other side even.</start_of_turn>
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The limb of the sciatic nerve is at the ankle of force, and its blood is worth the pain of the groin, when it is for blood that clots.</start_of_turn>
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And if the patient is in bed or in water, and he feels strange below the ankle, two fingers should be twisted there, for otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, do everything you can in every way, both from the front and from the back; it is better that you close it, for the wound is severe, and it is better to leave it alone with the hands of a master.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	If you do not find that the blood vessel opens when you twist two fingers there, if there is neither blood nor pus coming out at the small end, and if you are careful not to damage the nerves; do whatever you can to staunch the bleeding, then remove the ligature and put on cotton wool, and bind it. It is now healed.</start_of_turn>
des sainies de ventouse	of the air of the vacuum</start_of_turn
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this wound which is made with fire is in two ways: either it is with great fire or with fire; or the wound which is made by fire and by extraction of blood if it is made in twelve days from the commencement of the disease, of which one is all over the head and the other is at the collar; and two at the two costs of the collar; and the ventouse under the chin; and the ventouse of the two scapulae; and the ventouse over the nipples; and the ventouses at the two arms; and the ventouses of the two legs; and the ventouses of the two ankles; and this wound does not touch blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the flesh, for which reason it does not frighten me, as if we make a bleeding of a vein; and I do not consent to it except when it is administered, neither with great fire nor with fire, in any disease which comes from repletion, as long as all the parts are emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if necessity of disease compels him, or by custom, if the attendant should happen to speak carelessly in the beginning of the month or at its end, and every month in every tongue; for there are some who, when compelled to speak, have a weighty head; and there are some who find repletion and redness on their face, and on their head and neck, and dark circles under their eyes; and there are some who have a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swallowed it up, and spat blood; and there are some who dream of blood and navigate and die and other things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and even when it is already two hours since the pain began, we command the patient to vomit twice an hour.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The blood of the physician helps with the grief of the head … which comes from the black circles under the eyes; and it must not be used before the evacuation of all fat; for this ventilation is in lieu of the cephalic blood, and must not be used by those who are of a cold complexion or who have choleric temperament, because this causes great discomfort; and for this reason it must not be used except in those who have cold fevers.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And if the patient is conscious, if he becomes oblivious, then it is necessary to place the ventouse somewhat lower down in the region of doubt about his awareness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The wind blowing from the neck is in lieu of the blood of the head and the marrow, and for this reason it is worth at the utmost expansion of the pelvis, and to split the channel of the windpipe, and all, and to swell; and it must be borne since if it stays too firmly, it will cause indigestion or stomachache or pain.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The swelling of the neck is worth as much as the pains of the head, and swelling of the chest and spleen, and strangulation, and pain as the root of the teeth; and it is in lieu of the blood of the marrow; and you must command the patient to express his hand to prevent him from bursting an artery or vein from excessive pressure.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The windsings cause pain in the chest if there is illness of the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and similar illnesses which are in the mouth; and it is in lieu of the health of the two upper teeth.</start_of_turn>
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The windsings cause disease that comes from heat and swelling.</start_of_turn
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The swelling of the flanks is worth as much as three veins of the arm, because it draws blood from these large veins; and command the patient not to fill them too tightly, for they are full of marrow, and he knows the nerves and arteries
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The swelling that is on the buttocks is worth as many as blood clots at the foundation, and there are diseases of these; and it is recommended that the swelling be large and of hair, that it has plenty of space; and by chance, if it should burst, it makes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The veins of the legs swell widely open, for they draw blood from every part of the body, and cause ancient pains of the rains, and of the marshes, and of the bladder, and restore the flowers; and they are in place of the groin and the knee, and all of them grow blunt after a long time, and cause vomiting in various positions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the suction cup is that you put it on empty first, and then succeed gently, and put it firmly, and move it equally, and do not stop doing that until you see the mark of the blood and the swelling; then relax, and remove the suction cup, and take care of the position of the body, for there are some who have a hard time, and open wounds: if you only cut once, you can make large wounds, and a deep wound; and do it cautiously.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if it is not large, if you can, cut it twice: the first time to make the blood vessel small.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if it is not very painful, if you do it a third time; and when our veins swell with blood too much and too little, if we only suffer once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	If our veins bleed profusely, if we frequently renew the incisions; if it be without hope, if they are fiercely inflamed, and if it be that the cause of the wound is perceived, and it be in those who have thick skin and hard, and who have numerous pores, then you must apply the soothing and dissolving oil of rue marigold or bitter almond oil or pumpkin seed oil; or in yveir, cresson oil or ivy oil or chamomile oil or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	If the swelling is large and cold, take bitter oil, or balsam, or oil of rue, and the like.</start_of_turn>
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if it be on those who have strong veins and large pores, it is not permitted to apply oil, but it is permitted to wash afterwards with rosewater or cold water or vinegar or cucumber juice or porcelain water or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has moisture in his mouth, if he gets up easily, or from a thorn or from sumac, and from similar things.
