Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have excessive bodily humours rise from wine strong, or from water of hemlock, or from decoction of rue or chamomile, or from other such things; and do not take heed of any physician before the bath, but after the bath an hour or two; and do not sleep after the ventosation, and must keep awake when it is necessary to vent and when it is vented.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And keep warm those who are cold, and if they are too hot and inflamed; if you can give them cold things, such as pomegranate seeds and cabbage and lettuce readily, and other things; and eat barley broth, and broth of straw, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold complexion, if you give them honey syrup and fragrant wine moderate, which is between strong and new, and eat little broth, and eat barley broth and small oilseeds and herbs; and when he vents, he must drink more than eat; and it is not to give anyone vinegar or mustards before or after the ventosation, for it comforts the principal parts; and be discreet with it, but it is not to give anything but those who are hot drink it
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The wounds which are made to bleed are those which are made upon the liver, and upon the wrist, and the ankle, and upon the belly and the buttocks and the groin and the heel, for these members do not suffer from any wound upon their bones, and they do not do so for any other reason than to draw blood from a limb into another; as when we put them upon the nipples when they do not bleed; to reduce the viscosity which is in the limb; as when we put them upon the belly and the buttocks to strengthen the limb; and to stop the pain when there is swelling or a fracture, for the swelling attracts the swelling by its attraction or deserts the fracture from its place; and thus it makes elevation when it is put upon the liver and the wrist when there is retained moisture. And these compresses are administered empty without any other liquid, and never with plain cold water, as in cases of pleurisy; and in such a manner we fill the compress with hot water or water or such herbs as are suitable for that.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the compress administered with fire is like this:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And there are two large and half palms of barley and either cost the price of a thousand or a little more, like when a needle is pushed, and be of the kind that does not bleed the patient when put upon the limb; and in the middle is a rod of flax or iron, to put a bandage in place, and these are great and small according to the ailments and the severity of those who take them; for the blisters of the peasants are different from the wounds of the rich, and the leanness of the poor from the fatness of the nobles.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And you must put this sponge upon the limb: grasp the bandage firmly or with a line, and put it through the rod which is through the sponge, so that it does not burn the patient; and then put it upon the limb, and you must put either above the wound that we have said or below, so that when we see it, if it goes away, we will remove the sponge; and grasp the line as before, and do it often, if you are able.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the suction which is administered in the disease of pleuresin, at all sharpness, there is no vein or perforation, and it is only administered when it is clear of sharpness, and is put upon the limb only slightly; and that is its form.
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Suctions are only administered in limbs where we cannot put on suction cups because of their small size, such as the liver and gums, and similar things; and when the skin is stripped of hair, such as on the groin or navel, and other similar things; and the quality of the patient is such that when we find veins that are in soft, clear fluid without any perforation, if we take hold of them; we put on a drop of sweet liquid until they are plump, and have nothing in their stomachs; and then either drain the vein and the suction, then wipe the limb until it is red, and put on the veins; and when they are full and swollen, if it is possible to put on a suction cup, we put it on, for this is worth doing afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If this be not the case, if thou lift the limb easily, and then with some water, moist well, and then withdraw it; and if the limb remain too long in the water, if thou pour over it a cloth of linen in cold water, and place upon it, until the limb be extended; and if the limb be multiplied, if thou place upon it broken glass or nails, and suchlike things, until it be extended; or if thou takest out half of the nails from the limb, and leave them until they are burnt out in the limb, if thou wilt stop now; and if thou hast more to do, if thou take other nails.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	If the nails do not take hold, if thou frot the limb with fresh blood, or thou shalt thrust a needle into the limb until the nails are gone, and then place upon it, and as soon as they feel the blood, if they bleed; and when thou seest that they bleed, if thou pour over them upon a patch of aloes and rue, or charcoal, if they will stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This marks the beginning of the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is the restoration of fractures and the evacuation of pus
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Hear now, my dear son, that in this book there is something which no former writer has ever recorded, neither in book nor in letter; and for this reason it is strange in our land. For I have never learned of it from any other source than from the ancient books, or from my own studies and from custom; and I have described it in this chapter what is contained therein, and I have abbreviated it at the end, and I have made it clear the forms of the instruments which are mentioned, as I have done in the two preceding chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is necessary therefore that we say or write in the prologue of this book the sum of the word and the chapters or lessons that contain the true science, so that those who are proved worthy may learn it and teach others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twist or sprain occurs, if you must hasten the recovery of the patient on one side or the other, if nothing else hinders, if weakness of the limb, or youth, or old age; or if the tension is not very strong, or too cold; and mix cold urine, that is to say cold baths, and vinegar and oil, and do not drink wine, do not eat fatty foods, and do not eat too much meat which fills the veins with blood, until you are certain that the patient has recovered from the postoperative heat, or from the swelling of the limb.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to restore, if you must nourish the patient with meats that cause great nourishment, or if there is viscosity, such as barley flour in water, and rye, and testicles, and spleen, and fat, and fish, and wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For in part of nourishment, rest assure muscle and more easily will break through.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that bones broken by violence and decrepit ones cannot well take hold or knit according to their nature because of the drying of the limbs; neither those that are too tender, as bones of young children; but there is no remedy, you must rest on the broken bone a large support which has been proved to hold the limb together, until it becomes as strong as before; and do not move it in any way, for this reason it is necessary to nourish the bone with good meat, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are various in many ways.</start_of_turn>
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go through the bone, and others by bending, as with the size of a pen to write.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with a whole little fissure.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And indeed there is a sign of a fracture in its symptom and its own instrument in restoration; as it is remembered to come to its place. The fracture is known by the fact that the bone is twisted, and it opens well by pulling and pressing the hand; and when there is no twisting or touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no fracture; but it may well have twisting, or fissure, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it does not suffice that I tell you only that you must move the limb gently, but put on medicines that will come afterward, and then hold it steady now in secret.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And so it is that when the burst abscess bursts into the cavity, and it is the second part of the joint, it is necessary to put them in order equally, even as after an incision; and if after an incision the abscess becomes inflamed, if you leave no scar, until the abscess is calmed; then put it in order with the limb without violence or haste, and the burst abscess is easier to restore than to restore one which has pieces; then restrain it as before.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if there are broken pieces in the bone, if it be hands or feet, or at your hand if it be a small limb, or at two strings, or at a string and at your hand; and put the limb in its natural position, so that when the parts of the limb that have broken are freed, if you leave by all means the addition to the limb at the bone that you put, and keep that in your work does not cause the patient any lesion or pain; and adjust well the two ends of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And well he feels his hand if it seems to him that it is not well: if the swelling is great and does not constrain him too much, do not press so much as they do who make it come by their work of incision and contraction of the limb, as we have often seen.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is at rest, if the patient is diligent and does not move it, neither by day nor night, nor by turning, nor in any other way; and keep the limb firmly in place so that it does not cause him any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, if it is not at rest, you must put it in partial use so that he feels no pain; and keep it straight, so that no twisting arises until it is restored; and the quality of the limb will be as I have told you
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	The limb shall be set in different positions, small, large, and irregular in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small members, such as arms and thighs and the like: if you can cover them with soft and fine cloths; and for those that are large, such as bones and legs: cover them with a broad and hard cloth, for the large cloths embrace the whole large limb, and constrain it equally from all sides, so that there is no tension; then put on firm supports, three turns or four according to the limb, and constrain the hand one inch from the break, then go down from the break and constrain less, than the break then lets go one inch of the break; and soften the limb somewhat, as much as you take a large part of the limb that remains sound, then take away another cloth, and untwist the bandage from the break; then put back on the part below the break, and constrain moderately, not too strong not too little, as we said at the first hour above; then put between the supports cloths or bandages, so that they are even all around, and then tie everything up with strong bands, and put your pins well in place, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or abscess, put upon something soothing the abscess quickly, and which will stop the swelling; and leave it untouched for several days. Then strain upon your eyes, and let them be half of a broad thumb in breadth, or of a fist from which the nails are made, or of barley-corns, and let them be according to this figure.
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the staple which one puts on the fracture be greater and wider than the others; and be as long as it is necessary for the limb of little or great size; then strain upon the eyes as you did at the first hour, and then tie a thread loosely, as at the first hour on the fracture; the tighter the thread, the less; and it is necessary that the thread be moderate, neither too thick nor too thin, and be of linen wool. For if the thread is thick, like those fools who make their knots of silken thread, it is a great error, for the knot will not be equal if it is too subtle, and it will not hold well.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	If the patient is bruised by the nails after stripping in the flesh, if you put on stockings of linen or coarse cloth, so that it does not stain.</start_of_turn>
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the scraper, and the bone is fractured, I will speak of the cure of that afterwards.</start_of_turn>
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And if it cannot be restrained, these sparks must immediately break all the limbs which are broken first.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limb is great, it is not permissible for me to set these bones except after five days or seven, or more according to your situation after the wound has healed; and once this is done, the method of ancient plastering remains in use for restoring fractures, dislocations, and torsions: take some flour that adheres to the walls of a mill, and mix it with plenty of eggs, and make this confection, not too thick nor too thin, and use it. This is the common method of plastering that restores fractures in many situations, and even among women and young children, for it is neither too harsh nor too rough.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plastering that restores the fracture and dislocation and twist: take three barley grains and linseed and almond and alum and asphalt and gum arabic and mugwort, in the amount of x. three; mirre and aloes, in the amount of v. three; aleck, in the amount of viiij. three; and mix them into a powder, and mix them with eggs; if the complexion of the man is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and restores the broken bones immediately, and is worth more than many homes.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of plastering that is useful for dislocations: take mugwort and mustard seeds, 10; mastic gum and aloes, 9; acacia, 6; Armenian bole, 10. Grind them well and mix with water or plenty of eggs, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Other means of restoring joints and bones loosened from their sockets, and relieves pain coming from it, and makes the swelling diminish from the bone, and the fracture: take new linen, and moisten it in oil and on the skin, and put it on the limb.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These treatments do not restore them immediately, but they are good for calming excessive pain, and for strengthening bones; properly the pains
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Other method of support that restores fractured bones: take dry fig leaves and terrestrial heather leaves, grind together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	for restoring the fracture of the bone and for diminishing the remaining swelling.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of chamomile, chamomile flowers, violets flowers, barley flour, rue a three parts; grind them and mix with wine, and if the limb is swollen, mix with vinegar of coriander or vinegar, and apply it
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Other methods of restoring the limb are more forceful than the first, when an abscess hardens at restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take root of chamomile, seed of flax, balsam, melilot, and gentian, and violets and chamomile flowers, all of which make one part; and grind them, and mix with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ipocras writes in his book that nothing should be put on the broken limb except some wax and oil, and nothing else, and that it should be between two not too soft not too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen would have us put on the dry member something warm, such as mirre and aloes and incense and the like, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method of treatment that is worth for pain and lesions: take mugwort and chopped onions, or nails of oil, and gum, and mix them evenly, and grind them, and make a poultice of it.</start_of_turn>
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then loosen a little afterwards, and take care that the patient feels no pain, nor has the bone of the limb moved; if not loosen by hand days. If pain comes to the limb, or swelling, with rest or inflammation, if you hurry, loosen and oste the displacement now; and take a light bandage, and a wet sponge of sea, and immerse in water, and elevate the limb, until the swelling ceases and the pain is relieved; then leave the limb rest for an hour, and put on dry linen, moisten in water or oil of rose, and bind on a compress, until you are sure of the abscess has gone; and rest the inflammation of the limb, and be certain of the pain, then resume the gentle manipulation, and a little displacement, and do not strain it too much if before; and do it cautiously until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	If you see swelling, redness, pain, and swelling around a bone, and if you suspect a fracture, you must support and bind it firmly, as you did the first time.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	If it does not reappear after three days or four or five or seven days, do not leave it for twenty days, as we have seen; until the bruise has disappeared and the limb has returned to its normal position. Then increase the restraint more than before, and swell the flesh, as I said before; and if you see the limb drying out more than usual, do not hesitate to give warm water to drink. Every time you dislocate it, even every third day, cut the ligature and slash a vein. By this means you will shorten the swelling in the limb and restore its normal function.
des diverses manieres de brisure	various methods of fracture.</start_of_turn>
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many are the ways of fractures, and diverse are their figures, and the causes are diverse; for there are fractures that are made by the percussion of a spear, and the collar of bone is fractured all the way up to the syphus, which is the socket of the bone, as if made by nail or twist; and for this reason this kind of fracture is called a «fracture of the nail».
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or if the spear pierces the bone from below in a forward direction, and is called this kind of fracture «absolute»; and is the wound of these fractures great or small
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded percussion, or fracture or dislocation of the shoulder, or fracture of the bone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture that approaches the socket which is below the bone, or it is above the bone, this wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if a wound that has healed in the bone is as thin as a whisker, and if the wound is small, it is called a "caputre" break; and if the wound is made by a nail, or by a thorn, or by a similar thing, and if it brings into the piece of the bone which is below, and if the limb becomes limp as when the cauldron is heated over the fire; if between the nails.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this is what happens more often with moist bones, as with children; and there are many such fractures of this kind that the small pieces break away like stars; and I will speak of them later.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And thus, in all these ways of breaking, small pieces are loosened from them as with stars; and I will speak of it later.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary resemblance is known by that which when we discover the bone, and we wipe grease on it, if the black break appears.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the break, take care of the patient’s complaints; if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, loss of consciousness, swelling, bruising, fever, and other similar things, if there is no sense of doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	If you see no imminent danger, and you hope for health, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	When the fracture comes first to you, and that is in the armpit, if you can put the bone in place before the fourth hour of the day, do so.</start_of_turn>
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	If it is in this state, if you hurry to put the bone in place before the seventh hour of the day, even though the tissue of the bone is corrupted, the accident will come about as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if a bone fracture reaches the skin that covers the brain, if you must split the fractured part, take hold of the patient’s head and uncover the bone in every way you can, and on the form of the wound more deeply than you can; and if blood comes out from uncovering the bone, or from incisions, if there is aid in this, and if you fill the cavity with damp cloths soaked in rose oil; and rest the wound until the incisions are healed, and be sure of the bloodletting; then begin to bind up the bone in two ways: one way if the fracture is close to the tailbone, and that is the shape:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	and then there is another fracture which is greater than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And thus if you have a number of different-sized wounds, some wide and others narrow, and they are pointed or iron-hard; and over a wound that is slight, do not bleed the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is thick and hard, if you must pierce through, even if you administer wounds with sponges, do not make them penetrate deeper than the bone’s test; and must have under the point a margin or circle, that does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone; and you must have several of these, so that if the bone spur out in place of the thickness of the bone, if you have sponges for all the tests, this is the form of two methods of sponges:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing through the brittle bone is that you put one sponge on the bone, and turn your two hands until you sense that the bone is pierced; then put the sponge back in another place a little later, and do everything around, and close the incisions between the perforations, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you have brought the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have like pincers; and keep your hand away from the brain or the jaw.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced the bone, and treated, if it is possible, leave the dressing which is detached from the bone to all other instruments resembling an incisor, but make sure it is firmer and more flexible than the other incisor; and if it remains attached to nothing of the small bones, do not remove the fragments, if the bones rest lightly upon some instruments; then cure the wound with sutures and sponges as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of treatment is like that of the Galenicians, which is more famous; and the lord is very strong, and that is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, either the break or the protrusion, so that when you have uncovered that part, put on the saw, which is the shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	Do not cut too deeply, and if the part is between two ribs, if the cut is towards the bone; then hold a little mallet above, so that you can gently compress the bone together, and take care of the cloth which is around it; if it is against the bone, if the bone rests lightly, because we must support it well in its place, and not too tightly.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone breaks through the skin does not reach the flesh, cut the bone as little as possible by its under side; there will be small pieces remaining. If you leave the rough edges, they will irritate and wound the surrounding parts. Therefore you must have various quantities of scrapings, to bring to the surface of each piece the most convenient, according to the work and the figure of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If before there are great raisers of the flesh, and afterwards more subtle, and do not cease doing this until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	Concerning other capillary and subtle cuts, it is appropriate to bring the cause in accordance with its address; and this is something that is not easily learned by anyone who has not studied this art
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	If the wound is discovered, take I drapeil of linen, according to the quantity of the wound, and soak it in oil roset, and put it on the wound; then take I other drapeil doubled in II or III, and soak it in wine and oil roset, and put it on the first drapeil; and do this more gently than you can, that you do not tear the flesh, then administer by means of these sutures I other thread, and do not tighten it more than is necessary to hold the wound only; and leave it in I or II, until the bleeding stops, then take it out, and administer medicines as with roots of iris, and oatmeal, and powdered incense, and an apothecary, and similar things; and from these things make powder, and put it on the wound, and administer again appropriate medicines in the right order. And beware that the wound be well closed, that you do not leave it open, neither do you leave it to gather, for when it gathers upon the wound of the head, if it is crooked and twisted, it causes great harm to the patient; for when anything biting is put on the wound, if it is not held by these sutures.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take heed, therefore, if no other misfortune befalls the patient, as we have said, if there is any doubt or fear.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If black bile does not depart violently but only by the medicine we have put on, that some virtue has, if you can take a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and one drapel of glue, and apply them on the surface; then it will cure in the manner of cures that are appropriate, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Then the treatment in the way of treatment that it must be done, as long as it is sane.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	If one of the two parts is broken, if you can drink your little toe or pierce what you do not wish, and place the break inside your index finger and in the pouch by force, until it returns to its natural position; and do this gently, and beware that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the arm, and cannot come from below, you must know that you must place the forearm horizontally on the top of the radius like a large fist.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is of two parts, do it again, and hurry to restore the first part if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the swelling of the abscess has subsided, then bathe the head of the limb where the fracture is located with lint, if the break is in a part
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you bind it once more elsewhere if the break is there; and make the attempt so strong that it fills the hole in the bone.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say that no restorer shall mingle the tents in the burrow, and die each for himself.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	I do not seem to understand it, but it is fitting that they be mingled in the fashion of an egg yolk and powdered wheat; then leave the tent until the bone is firm and the cartilage is hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And never do we see goose feathers or hair in place of tents, and if indeed there is soft drape in the armpit, and it is held close, and blows the patient among them; or make him do whatever you see.</start_of_turn>
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if a wet dressing comes upon the neck while you are working, if you put some butter or cotton soaked in rose oil, or in some vinegar.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If abscesses do not come out, if you put on plaster by force, of hemp flour and incense powder, confirmed with egg yolk, then put on soft compresses, and do not bind tightly; and if the fracture is slight and it is broken into small pieces, if the extraction tool is useful, then close the wound, and heal with covering substances, such as plasters and ointments that are useful; and if there is no wound in the bone, if you heal the tent, and put on lead weights until it is healed
de la routure de la mandibule	De la routure de la mandibule.
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is fractured, without any wound, and the break is slight, and not deep, except for the teeth within, if one sees it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the break is on the outer side, bite your right index finger in the mouth of the patient; and if the break is on the left jaw, take your right index finger of the right hand, and touch the break lightly with the other hand, and hold it equal.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is displaced in general, if you must administer extension of the thumb by pairs, so that they are equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	If movement of the teeth comes about, or swelling, if the strain is from a thread of gold or silver or silk, then place a broken mandible cerote on, and place over it a double drape; and place over the drape a large sponge well made, or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the mandible, and bind it on the muscle as you wish, and command the patient to rest, and nourish with light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	If you see that the figure changes, if it is loosened at the third joint, and then reset it to its place; and place on it, powdered alum with a lot of eggs or wheat flour, after you have opened the cerote; and place over the alum dressing light linen, and if the dressing comes away, and the patient’s condition does not change, leave it as it is until it is healed; often it is healed in two weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if there is swelling of the gums comes, if you remember what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	If there is a fracture and wound together, repair that neither piece of the bone is broken; if subtle of the bone has instruments covering it close to this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	If the wound is wide, if the burn has flared up as you need.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you have solidified all these pieces, and there is no longer any displacement, if the wound is wide, and if there is need, put on some protective dressings that cover this area, in order to prevent pain, as long as it is necessary.</start_of_turn>
de la forcele	forceful
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceful breaking occurs many times before, on the shoulder, and it breaks in two ways: when it is broken and loosened in two pieces, or when there is damage and it is the most lightweight to restore; or there is a break with injury.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	When the breaking is with injury, if you have two attendants, let one hold the limb that feels the forceful break; and the other extend the neck towards the part; then put the break back in its place so that the form is as it should be, and there should be neither appearance nor pain.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you have to extend more, put under the shoulder of the patient a round ball of lead, or linen, of the size you need; and extend and hold the forcele, and strain the ball in your hand, so that you can put the break back in its place as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	If you do not manage to drive out the head of the dislocation, because it has gone deep inside, you must know that the patient lies groaning on his bed, and put on the shoulder, that is to say the middle ear, and hold the minister of the shoulder below, until the bone of the dislocation is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then address the fracture to your side, and if you find debris there, know that you must cut there; and force out the pieces gently, and if the bone will not join by any means, if it has gone into one of the incisors that you have; but that you put on the shoulder again, this instrument, to keep the jaw in place.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it appears like a spoon, and is not crooked, and should be as wide as it seems convenient, according to the size of the bone and the nature of the work; and has two holes, as you see, and one is large, and the other is small, as is the curve of the wound which you made when you treated the bone; and when you are certain of the apposition, if the wound is small, or if you doubt the apposition, if you employ the wound with bandages and sutures, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	If the wound is bleeding, if it is moist, apply oil of roses, almond oil and wine, and put on top.</start_of_turn>
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The stretching of the bone, when it is accompanied by wounds and pain, is that you put upon the bone a paste of powdered mill and egg-white, and put on light stockings, and put a sponge between the shoulder blades if you need to; then take a large bandage of a palm of a hand, and put on two layers of bandage over the stockings, and the paste; then take a needle with three threads of silk, and wrap around that bandage, so that the head of the bandage is between; and put the needle on the fracture, and turn the bandage over the collar, and take off the shoulder blades from the painful side; and support the part, and when you see that the ligature holds the fracture steadily, and that you clearly see that the needle does not move from the broken bone, if you reward each jerk, and if you hold it back; and make the patient rest on his back, and put under his armpit a little pillow to raise the shoulder; if you align the fracture with the alignment of the shoulder blade, or you bind the arm to the collar, and do not unbind it until it is well healed, which should take about twenty days; then repeat the packing, if you see that it is necessary, and strain and leave it alone, until it is restored; and it is usually restored in about eight days, and in less time for most men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Then resume the manipulation, if you see that it is necessary, and hold and restrain it firmly until it is restored; and it is restored in about twenty-six days, and in less time for most people.
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	When the shoulder is fractured or dislocated, do not move it except by touch; if the limb appears according to the fracture, and is restored according to its natural shape, in all ways that you can; then take out the bone powder with much egg white, pack lightly, and put on a double drape; then put on a broad and subtle wedge, a little wider than the shoulder, and keep the wedge firmly in place so that it does not move from its place; watch the patient carefully; and whenever it relaxes, if you tighten the wedge, and put it back in its place, rest the patient on their chest; and the shoulder will be restored in twenty days or less. And when that number is completed, if the pain subsides, for it is not bone that easily breaks.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone sticks forward, and does not yield at all, if it persists, hold the bone steady and do what we have said in the breaking of the forcele of soothing the abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	And if a piece of bone sticks forward, and does not yield at all, if it persists, hold the bone steady and do what we have said in the breaking of the forcele of soothing the abscess.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The weight is never broken in the middle, but this often happens; however, it often breaks from fear.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	When it is broken in the middle, if it declines downward, and causes the patient great pain, and lack of feeling, and spitting, and vomiting blood, and opens the jaws on the broken bone, and makes him groan.</start_of_turn>
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that if the patient lies so well on his back, and puts between the scapulae one cushion, then presses the scapulae, and reassembles the two costae with your hands, and discreetly put each one in every way you can, until the bone is as it should; then put on plasters and stamp below the staple of salt, or some lighter dust, and cover with a bandage, and bind on the broken bone, so that it does not move; and turn the bandage around the back, and strain immediately, and reward about an hour later, and if it relaxes, strain again; and if you suspect it is loosening, because of corrosion or swelling that comes from within, or pain or abscess, if you are in a hurry, and unfasten it, and scrape the plaster, and address what has come from the way of treatment; then remold the plaster, and strain until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	Of the fracture of bones
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Bones that break in the breast do not come out except at the shoulder blades and the head downwards, and do not bend out except because they are glassy; and the patient feels well at the inquiry as two.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	The restoration is when you put the fracture back in its place, as it should be.</start_of_turn
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then put the bandage, and hold it with a splint, if you need to.</start_of_turn
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the bones is downwards, if the patient feels great pain and tingling, as if of pleurasy, because the bone is pressing on the gut; and there is swelling, and vomiting, a great amount of blood, and that is a great grief of health, and the former has put in great effort.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if it is said that it is necessary to administer nourishing foods which cause the belly to swell, in order to drive out the bile which is in its ascent.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, except after vomiting has ceased and life is not in danger.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if there is vomiting, let it be so, if the patient is well.</start_of_turn>
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	They do not say that we must put on a ventouse on the limb for any reason, for this is like madness; however, there is doubt that the ventouse will not draw out the superfluous humors from the limb because of the weakness of the limb.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say of none of us that we must cover the limb with coarse wool soaked in hot oil, and put on tension between the ribs to keep the belly even; then either cure with the cure for pleurisin, meat and medicine.

And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear from the bone that points towards the belly, and there is doubt in the patient, if you can cut above the fractured bone, and put in place some instruments to hold the swelling; and then you must cut the bone, and drain it slightly, and then suture the two layers of the wound, if it is large, and treat it with bandages, until it is healed.</start_of_turn
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If blood spurts from an opening, put on moist cloths soaked in rose oil, and put on the limb; and treat while the limb is still in its place, and do not touch the surrounding area or it must, until it has stopped bleeding.
de la brisure dou col	of the fracture of the collarbone</start_of_turn>
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Never comes a sudden fracture of the bones of the collar, and often it rains; and the same with the thorn in the back.

de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	From the breaking of the thigh bone.

When the thigh bone is broken, if there is no immediate sign of improvement, there must be some cause for it; and there must be prolonged suffering, drooping of the spirits, and great pain to the limb, and swelling of that which is broken.</start_of_turn>
