And if he does not want to return to its place, if you administer strong extension; and that two assistants extend the arm, and hold it by two assistants, so that it does not move at the extension; then turn the arm from the shoulder, and when you have wrapped around a double-long and wide bandage; and when you look at the joint with its hand, if there is any oil on the joint for making it smooth, then join the joint together again, until it recovers; and when it is in place, put on dry plaster with egg-white, and strain it out, and bind the arm close to the patient, and leave it for some days, then take it off.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	If the joint is firmly in place, if you notice that it is not properly aligned, leave it as it is; and if you see that the joint does not mend well, repeat the manipulation of the limb and the joint, and leave it thus for some days, until it is firmly set; then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	If he feels pain after the joint has been set, and it moves, bathe and rub thoroughly, and press until it is eased; or place upon the joint a mutton fat nail, then leave it in place for a night, and the bone, and let the swelling go down. Then, when the swelling has gone down, gently rub the joint, and remove the nail; then enter or bathe again. Repeat this two or three times until the pain has gone. If you see that it returns to its place, place upon it a moist poultice soaked in urine, and hold it in place until it returns to its normal position.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand.
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the hand has loosened, and its return is laborious, more so than other joints in general; one must urgently restore it to its place, even if it is loosened, and even if the limb is swollen or there is an impending fracture.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	If you put the affected limb on a table, and extend the limb, look at it so that it rests on its natural position, and place the palm of your hand on the surface of the joint, and press until it returns to its normal position, you must watch to see if it is properly aligned; then put the affected limb back on the table, extending and bending it at the same time
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, let the patient place the back of their hand on the table, and the physician should place their hand over that part of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it comes back now, that is well; if not, if the strain of the supporting ligaments is appeased after the incision, and you leave it in its original position to recover.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot bear it, and you do not wish to set it again after a few days, the joint will become stiff; and do not harm the patient more than is necessary, for as long as the hands are relaxed, and do not move anything: since the nerves are cut, or the artery; if there is no other reason for moving except to cauterize, leave the case as it is, and by chance that is the only thing.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is at rest, if you place on the place that we have said, then strain and leave it for three days, then remove it and leave it be.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it cannot move well, and there is no pain, if there is warm moistness, and you rub it until it is healed
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the shoulder blades of the hand.
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Never is the thumb detached from the wrist but at the back of the palm or at the belly; then is the thumb extended, and the dislocation returned to its pouch until it returns; then sustain the head of the thumb, and guide it towards the part where it is joined; and leave it for two days, and then put it back as it was before; and do not tie it, as we have said, and do not move it, and tie it again; and do this often, until it is tight, and do the same if it is detached at the belly of the thumb, and do as you have done before, until it is healed; and do the same if it is detached from another part.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Because of the loosening of the scapula from the back.
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the scapula of the back or the neck is loosened, or if there are several loosenings, if there is no remedy, for the patient’s life is in danger.</start_of_turn>
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the sign is that the blood egestions spur in the opposite direction, you cannot hold it, and many times it makes the limb limp, or the two thighs or two arms or one leg limp; and many times the marrow turns black at three parts; the one that turns at the back is called "gilbosite": the cure is if the gilbosite is from childhood: if there is no cure or healing of the whole.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from sitting or from blows or from similar things, say the old physicians in their great words, or it bears no great profit; but I have abridged it according to my intention, and I have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the swelling that comes before the wound, there is no real health; and that which comes directly on the two costae, we cannot cure it except for what comes from behind, as I have said; and let the patient be stretched out on his face in one equal league, and let him be strained from his waist down, that he should not move; then I will put a cushion at the head of the bed, and another at the feet, and I will bind up the patient’s legs with a thread, and another I will put haincings and bands, and I will bind up his thighs; and two assistants shall know the threads, one at the head and the other at the feet, among the two cushions; and let them be well bound up, the cushion as I have said, and the patient shall put his palms on the spine until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	If she does not return by this treatment, take a tablet of three hands' breadth long, and sew it to the side; let the patient lie on his side, and put the head of the tablet beside the side, then put the middle of the tablet on the spine; and put the thumbs of both hands on the other head of the tablet, and press firmly, until it returns to its place; and if you see, if it turns at the wrist.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	If you see two veins at the wrist of the patient of a hand of great length, and two others below them, and between each pair of veins, a sow and a bandage, a palm of space long; and in each pair of veins, one puncture, or the wrist is corrected, and the veins are firmly held in place so that they do not move; and between each pair of veins, there is one vein turning back, so that the median nerve returns, and there are two small veins of a palm's length beside the return; and then the master puts the median nerve alongside the ulnar nerve at the elbow and the other median nerve alongside the radial nerve at the other elbow, and the attendants turn their thumbs to the whole length, and the master makes the spine even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	When it is even, if you put on a dry dressing with a lot of eggs, and then press, and then support with a tablet of three fingers' breadth, that will bring about the evacuation of the bile from the gall bladder and the part of the spleen that is painful; then bind with a thread, as we have said, and use the patient with a quiet reassurance until he is well; and if nothing comes to an end of the well-being, if you must administer soothing and calming medicines, with the support that we have said before; and never give a piece of lead, and never does it appear at the back of the shoulder blade, and take care that this is not a dislocation; for it is the bone that has opened, for which we must not have presumption: by chance comes death.
des dislocations de la hainche	hip dislocation
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	The joints of the hip and shoulder never dislocate except for dislocations alone, they do not come out if like other joints; and the joint of the hip is damaged according to three parts: front and back, and front and back; and the more it is damaged in front, the more it is damaged at the back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And thus it is known of dislocation that when the painful limb is joined to the flesh, if it is longer and the painful parts are greater than the healthy, and if the painful parts cannot double their knee at the fire; and it is the heat which is left from the incisions that brings the head of the shoulder back.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of this is that in these cases it is contrary to the former.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of this is that if the limb is well placed in accordance with the completion, though it is doubled, do not do so violently, for if you see it turn pale, do not delay, but hold it back, and keep it still.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of that one who has it behind, if he cannot expand his knee, cannot double it, and his leg is shorter than the other, and his ankle is softened, and his shoulder is dislocated at the root of the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	If this semblance of dislocation persists, if it is an old dislocation and does not go away of its own accord, there is no remedy; and I do not know that there is anything that can be done about it.</start_of_turn>
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in this case, if the dislocation is recent, and there are three ways of dislocation, if you are quick to return the joint, and stretch outwards and downwards, and move to the right and left; by chance it will return, and there is no need for any other remedy.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, it is necessary to support the limb strongly with two hands, or with one hand that is bound to the knee; and another minister extends his hand above in part as much as he can stretch his hands below his buttocks, then he grasps with a loop the limb above; and another holds the head of the limb; and they stretch upwards and downwards at the same time, until the painful part is lifted from the ground at one time, and remains suspended
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common in three out of four cases; and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, that is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If this is not the case, if it is possible to cure its semblance, when the dislocation is in the arm, you must first lift the patient over his side, then put the limb on the root of the bone, and the bone that is below the angulus, then extend the limb above the angulus and towards the forcele; then grasp the other hand of the patient and embrace the great bone of the painful limb, and extend it towards the front: if it returns to its place now; this method of dislocation is easier than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	If you do not tighten it in this manner, if you can tie the two feet of the patient together with a strong thread over the two nails, and over the two knees, and let the painful limb be extended two fingers more than the others; or hang it suspended from the top of a pole, or on the ground two arms long; then command one minister to embrace the head of the limb, and let another minister hang alongside the patient, who embraces the limb, because the joint is now returning steadily.</start_of_turn>
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	When the dislocation is loosened, if the patient is present, as we have said concerning those who have a dislocation of the shoulder, grasp the limb firmly just above the elbow and below the wrist; then place two fingers, one at the head and the other at the base, and insert one finger between the thighs of the patient in the shape of an arrow; and place moist cloths around, so that it does not bleed excessively, extend the thumbs ministering to him, and the patient places his hand in the same position as the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is well.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place the table there and press firmly as we have said concerning the dislocation of the shoulder, and keep the patient on the cost side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	When the dislocation is forward, if you must, extend the affected limb strongly, as I have said; and place your eyes above the painful area, then press with the other hand, and extend backwards towards the groin.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is loosened, if it does not manage to extend the limb downwards, do not lift it up from the earth, but know that it must remain as it was loosened at the outset; as we have said concerning the two thumbs; and be on the face, and stretch the limb as we have said before, and must press on the joint at the table; and it will be finished when the patient extends his leg, and they will be equal; then join the thighs, and put the dressing on, and keep the bandage tight, so that it does not move; and leave it for three days or four, then take it off, and put the dressing on again; and if you see that they are equal, if the bandage is tight, as before, and leave it for three days; then take it off, and let the limb rest comfortably, until it is comfortable
de la dislocation dou genoil	from dislocation of the shoulder.
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is discharged in two ways: that is to say, inwards and outwards, and behind; and do not discharge it forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And thus the sign is that you command the patient to bend his leg at the knee, and if he does not stretch it to his buttock, his bowels will be emptied; and restore all when you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and place your hand on his face, and put your thumb on his toes; then take his kneecap with your palms and draw it between your thighs, then bend the two costae of the kneecap; and another attendant extends his thumb, as long as the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he has well bent his leg lightly; and put on the dressing and make the limb firm at the buttock, and bind them together firmly for three days or four, then remove it. And do not trouble the patient any more, until the limb is comfortable.

de la dislocation dou talon	of dislocation.
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The talons never is esteemed, and never is fully discharged, always remaining somewhat moist and soft.

Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely drained, if you do thus, you must make the patient sit upright, and hold him firmly by the leg under the ankle; then pull the limb to your right hand, and then to your left hand twice, and extend it upwards, and hold it firmly; do this twice as we have said, with one hand pressing down and the other hand pulling the limb; if it returns, that is well; if not, repeat the work, for it will return; and if it cannot return, make the patient lie face down on the ground, and place a firm bandage between his thighs, and bind his genitals tightly, so that it does not bleed; then hold the limb with one hand or both hands, or with a support at the collar of the limb; and extend the toes equally, and keep the limb firmly between the patient’s thighs to retain the limb when it is extended; then put the thumbs equally on the dislocation with one hand and another supporter holds the limb firmly at the ankle, and the dislocation will return immediately.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	When it comes to a point, if you put on the plaster and stamp on, and the strain forms, and you bind the limb to the leg, and guard the nerves which are above the ankle behind, that the bands do not become too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the strain has subsided, if the tension is not excessive; then remove the bandage in a third or fourth part, and inform the patient of this for three days; and if he advances to this point, this is not certain except that he will recover.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he persists in this state, if you must force him, as we have mentioned elsewhere, until he is whole.</start_of_turn>
des dois	until he is whole.</start_of_turn>
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two bones are dislocated, if you can manage them well, it is a light matter.</start_of_turn
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the dislocation is in no other place but on the bone of the limb, then you must make the patient sit upright on one leg or on a table straight, and put your hand on what is open of these joints, then press your hand until it returns; and when it is even, and there is no opening, if you put on the bandage of the limb two fingers wide, then the strain forms, and leave it for three days, then remove it; and rest it until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	This text includes information about treating various medical conditions, including wounds and dislocations.
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When an injury accompanies a dislocation and it is seen to restore itself, many times it happens that the patient dies: if you do not show enough presumption in the treatment, if you are not skilled in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not merciful and compassionate and timely, do not be ashamed; and begin with soothing measures to the wound, and leave the patient in the hands of the Lord, if you do not see hope of recovery; and when you see hope, restore the limb to its place, as well as the wound itself; and when the limb is in place, administer soothing measures to the wound, and cure the injury, as it should be, with dried sponges; and if with the dislocation there is a fracture, and bones are fractured, if the bones are displaced, do as we have said in simple diseases; and avoid any path of fear, as I have said, for this is unprofitable according to your Creator, and for the preservation of your arm and body.
Amen	Amen.
